Speeches by Delegates from Various Countries at the Naval Conference: The U.S. Advocates a 20% Reduction, Britain Advocates Abolishing Submarines; Japan Expresses Opposition to Each; Washington Believes a New Agreement is Hopeless 40

(London) The naval conference, one of the most important conferences since the war, opened at 10:30 this morning in the Locarno Room of the British Foreign Office. British Prime Minister Baldwin first gave a speech welcoming the delegates from various countries and explained Britain's position. He then left the meeting, meeting with Acting Foreign Secretary Eden, showing the severity of the situation in Italy and Abyssinia. U.S. delegate Davis followed the British Prime Minister and spoke, explaining the U.S.'s attitude. Japanese delegate Nagano followed and spoke. Other speakers included Australian delegate Bruce, Canadian delegate Meighen, French delegate Corbin, Indian delegate Butler, South African delegate Dulanty, Italian delegate Grandi, New Zealand delegate Ball, and South African delegate Walter. Each delegation sent twelve people to attend the opening meeting. The speaking time was limited to five minutes. (9th Reuters Dispatch)

(London) The naval conference opened today. The U.S. advocates a 20% reduction in naval power, Britain advocates limiting submarines, Japan demands equality, and France and Italy oppose entering into long-term agreements. The U.S. firmly disagrees with Japan's demand for equality, so the conference is bound to become a stalemate. After speeches by the delegates from various countries, today's meeting adjourned at 11:45 AM and will reconvene at 10:30 AM tomorrow. (9th National Dispatch)

(Washington) Officials here heard the speeches of the delegates from various countries at the London Naval Conference today and were pessimistic, believing that the positions of Britain, the U.S., and Japan are too far apart and that a new treaty has little hope of being established. (9th National Dispatch)

(Tokyo) According to well-informed sources, Japan seems to agree with the proposal made by British Prime Minister Baldwin in his opening speech at the naval conference to conclude an agreement on the misuse of submarines. However, Japan will firmly oppose the proposal made by President Roosevelt in his letter to his chief delegate Davis to reduce the total tonnage of the navy by 20%, and will oppose the reduction in the quality and quantity of submarines. If Britain and the U.S. cannot agree on a substantial reduction in the quality and quantity of battleships and aircraft carriers, Japan may still demand an increase of 78,000 tons. (9th Reuters Dispatch)

(Tokyo) At the naval disarmament conference held on the 9th, British Prime Minister Baldwin's speech was the opening speech, and the essence of its content has now been shown to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs by the British government. Although his tone was extremely steady, he hoped to continue the main purpose of the Washington Treaty and establish a general agreement on naval armaments in the spirit of mutual concession, advocating the complete abolition or extreme reduction of submarines. Especially when an agreement cannot be reached, he advocates the implementation of qualitative restrictions on various warships, which is particularly noteworthy. Judging from this situation, the attitude of the British government towards this conference has not made any progress since the preparatory negotiations, nor has it produced any new meaning, and it is still far from the position of the Japanese government. Therefore, the future of the conference will inevitably have many difficulties. (9th Japan League Dispatch)

(Tokyo) Regarding the question of abolishing or prohibiting the misuse of submarines, which is part of the British proposal, the Japanese Navy has expressed its views, which are recorded as follows: The majority of representatives at the Geneva General Disarmament Conference have considered submarines to be defensive weapons, and the relative relationship with similar forces in other countries is extremely weak. Therefore, countries consider them to be necessary defensive forces based on their defensive position and geographical location. Especially in Japan's position, they are even more necessary. Therefore, we must resolutely oppose the abolition of submarines. As for the agreement to prohibit misuse, it is another matter. (9th Japan League Dispatch)

Speeches by Delegates from Various Countries 41

(London) The main points of the speeches of the delegates are as follows: British Prime Minister Baldwin said that Britain's position has been explained in detail at the 1932 Disarmament Conference and has not changed since then. The British government is still prepared to extend the principles of the Washington and London Naval Treaties and make necessary amendments to adapt to changes in the international situation and the needs of various countries. The current conference has two obligations: to continue the work of previous conferences and to strive to avoid the recurrence of unrestricted naval competition. The British government attaches great importance to the continuation of qualitative and quantitative restrictions and hopes to see a reduction in the types of large ships and large guns, and even more hopes to see the abolition of submarines. If the international community can reach a compromise on this, the world's naval construction expenditure will definitely be greatly reduced in the future.

The British Prime Minister continued, saying that preliminary talks were very valuable, and countries can now understand each other's special problems and difficulties. We should agree on some restrictions so that, on the one hand, countries can have room to cope with their special needs, and on the other hand, we can dispel the world's fear of naval competition. This is very important. The most expensive and most dangerous part of naval competition is the desire of countries to compete with each other on new types of warships. As for the submarine issue, if agreement cannot be reached on its abolition, there must be an agreement to prevent its misuse. The French and Italian governments can accept the provisions of the London Naval Treaty regarding the treatment of merchant ships by submarines in wartime. These provisions have long been accepted by the U.S. and Japan, so he hopes that unrestricted submarine warfare can be avoided in the future. Although some delegates may not agree with some provisions of the Washington and London Treaties, there is one undeniable fact: in the past fourteen years, there has been no naval construction competition that has harmed relations between countries as before. He firmly believes that if countries are prepared to make slight concessions in their demands for the sake of public welfare, an agreement that not only reduces tonnage but also enhances the world's sense of security can be easily concluded. (9th Reuters)

(London) Davis, Chairman of the U.S. delegation to the London Naval Conference, said in a speech to the delegates today that the U.S. does not intend to take the lead in naval competition, and said, "We do not want to increase the navy, but only want to limit and reduce it. Most of our current construction programs are to replace old ships, which is also consistent with this desire. The U.S. has stopped building warships for ten years. Even in terms of the existing construction plan, the strength allowed by the London Treaty to be achieved by the end of 1936 will not be achieved until 1942. We do not hope to exceed the restrictions of this treaty."

Before Davis's speech, he first read a letter from Roosevelt fourteen months ago. The President strongly stated in the letter that the U.S. does not want any naval competition, but hopes that the existing naval treaties can continue to be effective, and said, "The Washington Conference is a monument to the progress of human civilization. The London Treaty also recognizes that this good work should be promoted, and the reduction of the navy should be further expanded. The Washington and London Treaties are now not only a mathematical formula, and the ratio stipulated is based on the comparative needs of national defense of various countries. The main interests of various countries are not sacrificed, and the security between naval powers is not damaged. If these treaties are abolished one day, the principle of mutual security will be completely out of balance and will lead to competition in naval construction. The outcome is difficult to predict." Davis added that in order to achieve the goal of limiting international naval competition, amending existing treaties is also a method, otherwise, we should try our best to exchange opinions in a frank and friendly manner, so that we can find a way to mutual understanding, as a basis for the establishment of a more permanent and more extensive treaty in the future. (9th National News Agency Dispatch)

(Tokyo) The full text of the speech by Japanese Plenipotentiary Nagano at the opening ceremony of the Naval Disarmament Conference held today is as follows: Now that the Naval Conference is convened here by the five countries of Japan, Britain, the United States, France, and Italy in accordance with the Washington and London Treaties, the Japanese Plenipotentiary would like to express his gratitude to the British government for its efforts in various mediation efforts since last year regarding the convening of this conference. He also said that maintaining and promoting international peace is the consistent policy of the Japanese government, so the Japanese government has always sincerely participated in previous disarmament conferences and cooperated with the countries concerned. This conference also wants to achieve a fair and appropriate disarmament agreement, ensure the security of national defense of various countries, reduce the burden on the people, and at the same time attempt to promote world peace and friendship. However, the purpose of this conference is to determine the naval armament of the countries concerned after 1937 and to conclude a comprehensive new naval treaty. The Japanese government believes that when formulating this new treaty, we should determine the common limit that major naval powers in the world should not exceed their holdings, and we must reduce the offensive forces as much as possible as a fundamental measure, and prepare the defensive forces, in order to achieve the actual results of disarmament. At the same time, we must establish a situation of non-threat and non-aggression between countries, and this must be the foundation. The Japanese government really wants to achieve this kind of fair and appropriate disarmament agreement, in order to reduce the burden on the people of various countries and truly contribute to the permanent peace of the world. We firmly believe that this is the best way. Therefore, we follow the above policy, and with a spirit of love for peace, we are willing to work with the plenipotentiaries of various countries, with an open mind and frankness, and to devote ourselves to negotiation. In order to achieve the most just and reasonable new disarmament agreement, we will always sincerely cooperate throughout the process. This is what I want to express. (9th Japan League News Agency Dispatch)

(London) When the Naval Conference opened this morning, Italian Chief Delegate Ambassador Grandi gave a speech, first expressing his gratitude to the British government for its hospitality, and said, "After thanking the government for representing my country, I should personally thank British Prime Minister Baldwin for the friendly words he issued to us in the opening speech just now. We are now showing the same enthusiasm and friendship in order to live up to the elegance of Prime Minister Baldwin. The Italian government has always spared no effort to prevent the recurrence of the system of unlimited arms competition today. The Italian government is in the current difficult situation, and it has to be cautious, which is well known to you. And this dangerous situation is caused by the attitude of the majority of members of the League of Nations towards Italy, which is also undeniable. However, even though Italy is in this environment, it still attends the Naval Conference today, not only because we still adhere to the principles of limiting armaments and reducing armaments that we have insisted on for many years, and we are participating in the Naval Conference with this spirit as our goal. Since the conclusion of the Washington Naval Treaty, Italy has always hoped that the entire disarmament issue can be resolved in a fair and practical manner. But any solution is not easy to maintain for a long time, so we must gradually study various options and examine in detail the new problems that these various options may cause, in order to decide on a naval restriction plan that can be accepted by all countries. In short, the Italian policy is to prevent arms competition, and this is our consistent goal, and we will never give up." (9th Havas Dispatch)

After Baldwin's speech, the U.S. delegation nominated British Foreign Secretary Hoare as the chairman of the conference, and Naval Secretary Monsell as the vice-chairman. Following Italy, they nominated British Foreign Office official Hallman as the secretary-general. (9th National Dispatch)

U.S. Attitude Unchanged; Not Planning to Make New Suggestions Immediately 42

(London) The delegates from France, Italy, and the U.S. attending the Naval Conference visited British Naval Secretary Monsell at the British Navy Department today. Although there were talks in various aspects, there were no new developments. It is heard that the U.S. position has not changed significantly since the last naval conference. The U.S. is not prepared to make any new suggestions immediately, but will wait for Britain to initiate. Twelve people from each delegation will attend tomorrow's meeting, but later only seven people will attend. There will be no meeting on Sunday afternoon. On Tuesday, they will meet to discuss the procedures and appoint committees. The method is the same as the previous naval conference. The delegates from various countries all expect that there will not be many formal meetings held at the meeting place, because much of the work will be done in bilateral meetings in hotels. The delegates from various countries have now contacted each other to exchange opening speeches. (8th Reuters Dispatch)

U.S. Secretary of War's Annual Report Advocates Expanding the Air Force to Reach 3,000 Aircraft 43

(Washington) In his annual report to President Roosevelt today, Secretary of War Dern recommended strengthening the Army's reserves and advocated increasing the Army Air Corps to increase the number of warplanes to 3,000 within five years. The Secretary of War strongly urged maintaining the current regular army strength and increasing the number of officers by 2,000 to reach 14,000. The Secretary of War also praised General MacArthur's talent and perseverance and recognized that the Army's progress in recent years was due to his contributions. According to the plan, MacArthur recently resigned as Chief of Staff and was transferred to the position of U.S. military advisor to the Philippines. (8th National News Agency Dispatch)

Another Riot in Cairo: Infantry and Cavalry Deployed for Defense, Fears of Escalation 44

Cairo: Reports indicate that the recent riot resulted in 18 injuries and 75 arrests. Today, the cabinet authorized the police to open fire on demonstrating crowds. The government also announced the closure of Cairo University and other schools. Students burned four streetcars today, and demonstrators waved revolutionary flags. Another group of 2,000 people defended the commercial school, with students throwing bricks at the police. A third group marched near the British Club. The British police chief, Russell, ordered them to disperse, but they ignored him. He then charged into the crowd, single-handedly knocking down over a dozen rioters. The remaining crowd was dispersed by police reserves. (National News Agency dispatch, 8th)

Cairo: Students and troublemakers not only set fire to trams and threw stones at police today, but also chopped down trees and smashed streetlights. The police fired warning shots, and the crowd dispersed. However, the wreckage of vehicles and other debris was strewn across the streets. The Minister of the Interior has now announced a ban on all future demonstrations. The police may use firearms when necessary. The authorities will take all possible measures to protect lives and property. The disturbances in Cairo and Egypt in recent weeks are the result of the Nationalist Party's opposition to the pro-British stance of the Egyptian Prime Minister and dissatisfaction with British policies towards Egypt, especially those related to the Egyptian constitution. There are fears that today's riots may escalate, so Egyptian infantry and cavalry have been ordered to deploy for defense. (Reuters dispatch, 8th)

Anglo-French Paris Conference: Decision on Italian Plan, Peace Based on Mutual Non-Humiliation, Optimistic Atmosphere in Rome 45

(Paris) Today, Britain and France agreed to give Mussolini another opportunity to reach a settlement with Abyssinia based on the League of Nations' conditions. If Mussolini refuses, Britain and France will jointly intensify sanctions against Italy to economically cripple the country. This agreement is the result of a meeting between French Prime Minister and Foreign Minister Laval and British Foreign Secretary Hoare. Previously, Mussolini had rejected the peace plan tentatively proposed by the two countries. However, Laval and Hoare were undeterred and decided to formally present it to Italy in a near-final ultimatum, while also submitting the proposal to the League of Nations. Furthermore, Hoare and Laval reportedly agreed to find a way to bring Germany back into the League of Nations in February next year and to revive the issue of limiting land and air armaments. If Mussolini or any member of the League of Nations rejects the Anglo-French peace plan, then the peace talks will be abandoned, and further discussions will be postponed until Mussolini seeks peace. This plan does not stipulate the suspension of sanctions during the peace negotiations. Diplomats say that the complete coordination between Britain and France since the outbreak of the Italo-Abyssinian dispute is truly embodied in this plan. (National News Agency dispatch, 8th)

(Paris) French Prime Minister Laval and British Foreign Secretary Hoare met for over two hours this morning, continuing discussions in the afternoon. They have finalized an agreement on a plan to resolve the Italo-Abyssinian War. The British community here expressed moderate optimism at the end of this morning's discussions. The British now believe that Mussolini will have to consider this plan as the basis for judgment, as it is neither pro-British nor pro-French, but 100% aligned with the interests of both central powers. At the end of this morning's meeting, those responsible stated that the two officials had worked painstakingly to formulate recommendations, demonstrating their sincere desire to find a basis for negotiations as soon as possible to submit to the Italian government and the League of Nations. British Foreign Secretary Hoare has been advised by doctors to rest and departed from Paris for Switzerland tonight. (Reuters dispatch, 8th)

(London) It is reported today that the Anglo-French "final peace proposal" will be submitted to Italy, Abyssinia, and the League of Nations on Tuesday, and that Emperor Haile Selassie and Italian Prime Minister Mussolini will be asked to formally respond before the League of Nations' Committee of Eighteen meets on Thursday, so that the Committee can conduct discussions based on these responses. The British Cabinet will meet tomorrow to approve the final form of the plan regarding the imposition of an oil embargo on Italy, and then it will be submitted to the governments of Italy and Abyssinia. (National News Agency dispatch, 8th)

(Rome) There is an optimistic atmosphere here today regarding a settlement of the Italo-Abyssinian dispute. It is said that Mussolini's tone in his address to the Senate will be more moderate, making the Anglo-French efforts to resolve the East African war hopeful. (National News Agency dispatch, 9th)

(Rome) The Senate held its first meeting today after the summer recess. The Crown Prince and other prominent figures were present. Speaker Federzoni declared that the presence of these dignitaries showed the world the unity of Italy, government and people. Subsequently, the Senate passed a resolution expressing its unwavering confidence in Mussolini. Mussolini's reply was very brief, saying that he would do his utmost to protect Italy's interests in Europe and Africa. (Reuters dispatch, 9th)

Anglo-French Joint Communiqué

(Paris) Laval released an Anglo-French joint communiqué to the press, which stated, "In the spirit of compromise and the friendship between Britain and France, Foreign Secretary Hoare and I have found a solution for a friendly resolution of the Italo-Abyssinian dispute. However, this basis is not yet ready for publication. The British government has not yet been informed of the basis we have agreed upon. After the British government accepts this basis, we will then submit it to the two parties involved, Italy and Abyssinia, and the League of Nations. In short, we are in complete agreement on the desire for a swift, peaceful, and honorable resolution, and we are both satisfied with the results achieved in this discussion." (Havas dispatch, 8th)

British Cabinet Meeting

(London) The Cabinet will meet this afternoon to discuss the content of the peace plan agreed upon by Foreign Secretary Hoare and French Prime Minister Laval in Paris. If approved, they will indicate the procedures for delivering it to Mussolini, Emperor Haile Selassie, and the League of Nations. It is reported that Emperor Haile Selassie has not been formally informed of the peace plan during the discussions by British and French experts in Paris. The prominent British politician Austen Chamberlain recently stated firmly in the House of Commons that any solution deemed acceptable by the League of Nations must be accepted by Abyssinia, as Abyssinia is not to blame in this war. There is no clear sign of agreement with this view in official circles, but some non-official quarters consider it important. (Reuters dispatch, 9th)

(Paris) After the British and French Foreign Ministers reached an agreement on a plan for the peaceful resolution of the Italo-Abyssinian dispute today, British Foreign Secretary Hoare left Paris at 8:00 PM for St. Moritz, Switzerland, to rest. British Foreign Office expert on Abyssinian affairs, Peterson, returned to London at 8:45 PM to present the plan to British Prime Minister Baldwin for review. If Baldwin approves the plan, Peterson will return to Paris tomorrow night to submit the plan to Italian Prime Minister Mussolini and ask for a response by December 12. British Foreign Office Under-Secretary Josias, who came to France with Hoare, will remain in France for several days in a private capacity. French Foreign Office officials believe that the plan drafted by Britain and France should be acceptable to Italy, as this plan makes as many concessions as possible to Italy within the limits allowed by the League of Nations Covenant and the will of Emperor Haile Selassie. (Havas dispatch, 8th)

Contents of the Anglo-French Plan

(Paris) According to the Havas News Agency's diplomatic correspondent, the main points of the plan for the peaceful resolution of the Italo-Abyssinian dispute agreed upon by Britain and France today are as follows:

(1) Grant Abyssinia free navigation to a port on the Red Sea. This port may be the port of Assab in Italian Eritrea. If Italy refuses to cede it, Britain may consider using the port of Zeila in British Somaliland as Abyssinia's outlet to the sea.

(2) Cede most of the Tigray province to Italy.

(3) Within a large part of southern Abyssinia, Italy will enjoy full rights. This territory includes the Ogaden region and the colonial zone west of that region, with its borders extending north to 8 degrees north latitude and east to 36 degrees east longitude. In this colonial zone, the Emperor of Abyssinia retains nominal sovereignty, but it is governed by Italy.

(4) The part of Abyssinia inhabited by the Amhara people (i.e., the main part of Abyssinia) remains independent, but the Emperor of Abyssinia may request economic assistance from the League of Nations. This economic assistance was originally proposed in the recommendations of the Five-Nation Committee of the League of Nations Council, but the full authority of the Italian representative under the Five-Nation Committee's recommendations has now been revoked. It is reported that the most thorny issue during the discussions between the British and French Foreign Ministers was the issue of the affiliation of the holy city of Axum in Abyssinia, as Axum is located in the Tigray province and has been occupied by Italian troops, and Abyssinia is unwilling to give it up. After Laval and Hoare discussed the results, they advocated recognizing Axum as a residential area for the Amhara people of Abyssinia and should be kept as part of an independent Abyssinia. The above Anglo-French proposals are expected to be sent to Italian Prime Minister Mussolini for review tonight or tomorrow. The Foreign Office here hopes that Mussolini will respond by December 12, the date of the meeting of the Committee of Eighteen. If Italy's response is satisfactory, Italian representative Aloisi may go to Geneva to negotiate a peace agreement, at which time Britain and France can request the Committee of Eighteen to postpone the passage of the resolution on the oil embargo. (Havas dispatch, 8th)

(Paris) Regarding the plan for resolving the Italo-Abyssinian dispute agreed upon by Prime Minister Laval and British Foreign Secretary Hoare, the general content has been detailed in another telegram from this agency. According to the Paris Echo newspaper, in addition to the Italian port of Assab or the British port of Zeila, the French port of Djibouti can also be regarded as one of Abyssinia's outlets to the sea if necessary. As for the land in Tigray province, although it will be ceded to Italy, the holy city of Axum will still belong to Abyssinia and should be connected to the main part of Abyssinia by a corridor. In addition, the Ogaden region and the Danakil region should also be ceded to Italy. Within the southern colonial zone, a company registered in Italy should be established under the sovereignty of the Emperor of Abyssinia to carry out reclamation and set up a police force to take responsibility for security in that area. At the same time, the Emperor of Abyssinia should sign a mutual assistance treaty with the League of Nations, the content of which should be similar to that advocated by the Five-Nation Committee on September 18, and the Emperor of Abyssinia should hire foreign advisers to implement the mutual assistance plan, and Italian advisers should of course participate. Regarding this matter, the French Ministry of Foreign Affairs has also recently issued a communiqué, which briefly states that "Although Prime Minister and Foreign Minister Laval and British Foreign Secretary Hoare have found 'a plan that can be the basis for a friendly resolution of the Italo-Abyssinian dispute,' this plan has not been submitted to the governments of the countries concerned, so now is not the time to publish it. Any news about the content of this plan published by other newspapers should be regarded as speculation." (Havas dispatch, 9th)

(Paris) According to well-informed French sources, the peace plan set this time by French Prime Minister Laval and British Foreign Secretary Hoare caters more to Italy's wishes than any other plan set before. The entire Tigray province, except for the holy city of Axum, and the Ogaden and Danakil regions will be ceded to Italy. Italy will also obtain colonies capable of accommodating 1.5 million people. It is said that Hoare has already agreed to cede land limited in the north by the 8th degree of latitude and in the west by the 36th degree of longitude, reaching south to Ganya and the British Egyptian Sudanese border. This is twice the amount originally agreed to by Britain. Abyssinia will obtain the port of Assab and a corner of land to the sea. If Italy refuses to cede the port, Britain is still willing to cede the port of Zeila in British Somaliland to Abyssinia. As for the Amhara and Woggera provinces of Abyssinia, the King should request protection from the League of Nations, which will assign a technical committee including Italy to handle this matter. This proposal has been sent to British Prime Minister Baldwin. French circles all believe that the British government will accept it, and then a telegram will be sent to Italy and Abyssinia, asking Mussolini to respond before December 12. (Reuters dispatch, 8th)

Japanese Authorities Plan to Dissolve the Omoto Sect 46

(Tokyo) The authorities' investigation of the Omoto Sect's executives concluded on the morning of the 8th. The sect has a total of 200,000 followers. Those investigated were all executives. The prosecuting authorities have taken a firm stance because the sect has committed disrespectful acts twice. They are now gathering evidence and plan to issue an order to dissolve the sect within days. (Nichi-Ren dispatch, 9th)

Soviet Union Prepares to Observe Next Year's Solar Eclipse 47

The Soviet Union is actively preparing to observe the total solar eclipse in 1936. The Pulkovo Observatory has organized three survey teams. Astronomers from the United States, Italy, and Britain have requested to participate. In addition, the Nanjing Observatory recently sent a letter asking whether Chinese astronomers can go to the Soviet Union to participate in the solar eclipse observation. A new observation pavilion has been built near Moscow at the Kuchino Observatory, which is a Soviet innovation. After several tests, the pavilion has proven to be highly suitable and is not inferior to foreign pavilions, while being simple in structure and convenient to use. (TASS dispatch from Moscow, November 14)

International Commercial Telegrams

Reuters Special Commercial Telegram, December 9th 48

Gold and Silver

British Gold: The London gold price today was 141 shillings and a halfpenny, down one penny.

British Silver: The London silver market was quiet today. Prices are not expected to change much, but the actual prices cannot be determined without receiving a telegram from London.

Exchange Rates

British-American: The London foreign exchange market continued to be stable this morning. The US-British exchange rate fluctuated slightly, opening at $4.93125, up .0125 from Friday's closing. Within the first hour, it fell .00625, and then fell another .0125 at noon to $4.919375, after which there were no changes.

British-French: Opened up 12 points to 74 francs 674 francs 66, then no change.

Cotton and Wheat

American Cotton: The New York cotton market opened stably, with some prices unchanged and others down slightly. Trading was extremely quiet, awaiting the government's estimate. There was heavy rain in the western cotton belt, which is expected to damage the cotton in the fields. In addition, the stock market continues to be strong. These are all factors that are beneficial to the bullish side.

British Cotton: The Liverpool cotton market was stable today. Merchants are awaiting the release of the US government's estimate. At 1:00 PM, the January contract was 6.46, up two points.

British Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market was stable due to good weekend reports from the US market and a private wheat production estimate that was beneficial to the bullish side. The larger total amount of wheat shipped worldwide in the past week and the slight increase in local inventories did not generate interest. At 1:00 PM, the December contract was up .625 to 5 shillings 11 pence 875. Feed grains were stable.

American Wheat: The Chicago wheat market opened slightly higher due to better telegrams from Liverpool and a private wheat production estimate that was beneficial to the bullish side. Prices stabilized after opening. Feed grains opened slightly higher due to rain damage and poor quality.

Rubber

London: The London rubber market was stable today. The April-June contract opened unchanged at 6 pence 4375. At noon, it rose .0625 to 6 pence and a half.

New York: The New York rubber market opened stably, with no change in prices. Trading was light. After opening, prices were not significantly different from the opening.

Securities

New York: The bullish market conditions in the New York stock market on Saturday and Sunday resumed and were at their most intense today. Copper mining stocks were strong, public utility stocks were stable, and there was some profit-taking later, but sentiment was strong. Prices are as follows:

(Nanjing) Dr. Stampar, an advisor to the Economic Commission, returned to Nanjing after investigating Yunnan and proposed the establishment of a Health Experiment Station in Kunming, as well as schools for women's and infant health, midwifery schools, nursing schools, health experiment institutes, hospitals, medical relief, school health, and health education. He also proposed industrial hygiene and environmental hygiene work in the Gejiu tin mining area. Shen Baixian Discusses the Huai River Diversion Project 59

(Zhenjiang) Shen Baixian, after inspecting the Huai River diversion project, returned to the province and stated that the progress of all sections of the project was excellent, especially the Xingdong-Fupu section, which was progressing the most smoothly. The total amount of work completed has reached 160,000 units, and if the weather is clear, it can continue to increase. It is expected to be completed as scheduled by the end of April next year. (Special dispatch, 9th)

Laborers from Outside the Pass Return Home in Droves 60

(Tianjin) All road earthworks outside the pass have been completed. Due to the winter shutdown, laborers are returning home in droves. Zhangzhou and Xiamen: Strong Opposition to Rice Tax 83

Xiamen Faces Food Shortage; Rice Merchants Completely Suspend Operations

Xiamen Dispatch: The Fujian Provincial Government began collecting rice tax in the Zhangzhou area on December 1st. The Zhangzhou Longxi Tax Bureau established a branch office for the Zhangzhou area rice tax, with the Tax Bureau Chief Wu Qianyao concurrently serving as the collection director. On the 1st, collection officers were dispatched to Shima, Fuhe, Gangkou, Shimei, Fuguan, Chengnai Port, Haicang Xiaogang, and other key locations on land and water to set up tax collection points. Rice merchants in Zhangzhou and Shima suspended exports on November 26th because the tax bureau agreed to temporarily postpone the collection until next month. Therefore, from the 26th to the 30th, 3,000 bags of rice were still exported. After the tax collection was implemented on December 1st, rice merchants immediately suspended all operations and engaged in hoarding. Rice prices in the Zhangzhou area have risen instead, from 8 yuan to 8.45 yuan per shi (100 jin) [approximately 50 kilograms]. Cai Zhuchan, Chairman of the Longxi County Chamber of Commerce, Lin Miaoqing, Chairman of the Shima Chamber of Commerce, Shang De, Chairman of the Haicheng County Chamber of Commerce, and Yang Zhishan, Chairman of the Changtai Chamber of Commerce, jointly telegraphed the Provincial Donation Supervision Committee on the 3rd, requesting them to consult with the Provincial Government to abolish the rice tax. More than 20 public organizations in Zhangzhou and Shima also issued a joint telegram on the same day, earnestly requesting the abolition of the rice tax.

Due to the suspension of rice shipments from Zhangzhou, Xiamen's total rice reserves as of the 5th were approximately 300,000 jin [approximately 150,000 kilograms]. The daily demand for rice is 60,000-70,000 jin [approximately 30,000 - 35,000 kilograms]. It is estimated that the city will run out of rice in about five days. The Rice Industry Association specifically requested the Chamber of Commerce to convene a general meeting to discuss relief measures. The Chamber of Commerce convened a general meeting of representatives from various trade associations at 4:00 PM on the 5th. More than 40 representatives and all members of the Chamber of Commerce's executive and supervisory committees resolved as follows: (1) The resumption of the rice tax in Zhangzhou violates laws and regulations and harms people's food supply. Farmers in Zhangzhou are suspending operations in protest. The city's food supply has been cut off, causing deep concern. A resolution was made to telegraph the central and provincial governments in the name of the general meeting, requesting the abolition of the rice tax in Zhangzhou. (2) According to the report of the rice industry representative, the city's food supply is only sufficient for five days due to the suspension of operations in Zhangzhou. A resolution was made on how to seek relief: 1. A request will be submitted to the City Party Headquarters to convene a general meeting of representatives from all sectors to discuss solutions as soon as possible. 2. A letter will be sent to the Rice Industry Association, ordering all members not to raise rice prices. A telegram will also be sent to the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Finance to appeal for assistance. The telegram to the Executive Yuan states, "To Kong [Xiangxi], Acting President of the Executive Yuan, and Kong, Minister of Finance: The resumption of the rice tax in Zhangzhou not only hinders agricultural development but also violates the central government's clear orders to abolish excessive taxes and the Executive Yuan's instructions that all compulsory collections from the people by central and local governments must first be decided upon in principle by the Central Political Conference and reviewed in content by the Legislative Yuan before they can be established. Farmers in Zhangzhou are protesting and suspending operations. The city's rice supply has been cut off, while imported rice cannot be imported due to foreign exchange issues. The city is facing a food panic, and there is deep concern. We earnestly request that you telegraph the Fujian Provincial Government to immediately suspend the tax collection to uphold the law and maintain the people's food supply. We await your instructions with the utmost urgency. Xiamen City Chamber of Commerce, All Trade Associations of the City, humbly request." (December 7th)

Fuzhou: Financial Relief Urgently Needed 84

--Southeast Bank to be Reorganized--

Fuzhou Dispatch: Since the Southeast Bank and Tianji Money Shop went bankrupt successively, privately-run money shops have also withdrawn their banknotes from circulation, resulting in a sudden reduction of 2 million yuan in the amount of money circulating in the market and a severe tightening of credit. The Minhou County Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Ministry of Finance, requesting permission to order the Fuzhou Central Bank to allocate 1 million yuan for merchants to use as collateral for loans, using real estate as security, to facilitate financial turnover. Yesterday, a reply was received from the Ministry of Finance, stating that the establishment of a real estate mortgage bank was under overall consideration, but allocating 1 million yuan from the Central Bank for real estate mortgages was inconsistent with the bank's regulations and could not be approved. Currently, the Chamber of Commerce believes that with the Lunar New Year approaching and merchants needing to settle accounts, the entire commercial sector will be paralyzed if finances cannot be activated. It has been decided to discuss relief measures with banks and money shops again within the next few days, which must be implemented by the Lunar New Year at the latest.

After the Southeast Bank suspended operations, the provincial government established a reorganization committee to liquidate debts. For nearly a month, there has been no news of the bank's bills being honored. A few days ago, Chen Ticheng, Chairman of the reorganization committee, flew to Shanghai with Xu Fu, Director of the Provincial Finance Department, to contact the banking industry for assistance and discuss the reorganization plan of the Southeast Bank with Li Qingquan, a director of the Philippine China Bank. He flew back from Shanghai the day before yesterday. It is reported that considerable progress has been made. Regarding the reorganization, the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications have agreed to transfer 300,000 yuan of the Southeast Bank's collateral to the two banks. The reorganization committee has also recovered 300,000 yuan in debts owed to the Southeast Bank, totaling 600,000 yuan. It is hoped that part of the bills can be honored within the next few days. Regarding the reorganization of the bank, Chen Ticheng and Li Qingquan discussed the possibility of reorganizing it into a Construction Bank, similar to a construction bank corporation, specializing in investing in mining, road construction, electricity, and water conservancy projects in the province. However, the specific measures will have to be discussed in detail after the reorganization of the bank is completed.

At the beginning of the implementation of legal tender in the city, prices once increased. Chen Ticheng, Director of the Construction Department, ordered the Minhou County Chamber of Commerce to convene representatives from various trade associations to investigate the situation. If necessary, a price evaluation committee would be organized to determine price standards. In recent days, the Chamber of Commerce has convened responsible persons from trade associations of daily necessities to inquire about the situation. They all said that the economy was sluggish, purchasing power was weak, and financial turnover was tight. Shops were selling at low prices to clear out inventory. There was no reason to raise prices. As for the price increase of kerosene and flour, the source of supply was the standard, and it was not the deliberate price increase by the merchants in the city. The Chamber of Commerce believes that it is true and has replied to the Construction Department, stating that there is no need to organize a price evaluation committee. (December 7th)

Guangdong Province: Levying Tax on Imported Fruits; Tax Rate is 30% of Value; Restricting the Dumping of Imported Fruits 85

Guangzhou Dispatch: Guangdong Province is originally a fruit-producing area. Fruits such as lychees, oranges, pomelos, peaches, and plums are all fine products. Among them, Chaozhou mandarin oranges and Xinhui oranges are the most abundant. However, in recent years, farmers have not paid attention to planting techniques, and the soil has not been properly cared for. As a result, soil fertility has been exhausted, and production has decreased. This has caused great losses to rural by-products. At the same time, due to the decrease in local fruit production, foreign fruits have taken the opportunity to be imported. Up to now, imported fruits account for a large portion of imports. The authorities have specifically implemented a tax on imported fruits to restrict them and promote the sale of local products. The tax on imported fruits has been announced by the Finance Department and will be collected starting from the 6th of this month. The tax rates for imported fruits are as follows: "According to the review by the Finance Department and the Construction Department, regarding the case presented by the Chaozhou-Meizhou Customs Superintendent to prohibit the dumping of Dutch fruits in Guangdong, this Department, after review, determined that a special tax of 30% should be levied on all coconuts, raisins, and other unnamed dried and fresh fruits imported from Nanyang. This was jointly submitted to the Guangdong Provincial Government and forwarded to the 197th Political Conference of the Southwest Political Affairs Committee of the National Government for approval. This Department issued General Order No. 5215, instructing all special tax bureaus for imported agricultural products to comply with the order and post it for public notice. Now, upon reviewing the current regulations for the collection of special taxes on imported agricultural products and miscellaneous items in Guangdong Province, it has been stipulated that apples, coconuts, Golden Hill oranges, lemons, grapes, and Luzon mangoes (the above fresh fruits, in addition to the provincial Chen Fresh Vegetable and Salted Goods Row fee, are taxed at 9.06 yuan per unit) Siamese pomelos, coconuts, betel nuts, tomatoes, unnamed fresh fruits, dried plums, dried apples, coconut shreds, American pine, hairy fruits, yellow branch dried fruits, western branch dried apricots, large and small canned olives, canned miscellaneous fruits, dried chestnut meat, large raisins, almonds (dried chestnut meat, large raisins, and almonds are subject to the Beijing Fruit and Seafood Donation, actually charged at 9.6 yuan), and unnamed dried vegetables are all taxed at 12 yuan per 100 yuan of cargo value, which should have been followed and enforced. Now, a special tax of 30% will be levied on all coconuts, raisins, and other unnamed dried and fresh fruits imported from Nanyang. All kinds of imported fruits stipulated in the previous regulations should be changed to 30% together to facilitate inspection and prevent dumping. The original 2.94 yuan deducted for apples, coconuts, Golden Hill oranges, lemons, grapes, and Luzon mangoes for the Provincial Chen Fresh Fruit Row fee is no longer deducted as the fee has been abolished. The 2.4 yuan for dried chestnut meat, large raisins, and almonds is still deducted for the Beijing Fruit and Seafood Donation, in accordance with the approved calculation, in order to comply with the fixed plan. In addition to submitting a report and issuing separate orders, this is hereby promulgated so that all merchants and people in the jurisdiction are informed and must comply with the above matters and report and pay the tax separately from December 6th of this year without violation." (December 5th)

Economic Essays 93

Edited by Tang Qingzeng

Labor-Capital Coordination (Continued) by Zhu Tongjiu

IV. General Methods of Labor-Capital Coordination. There are three methods of labor-capital coordination:

(1) Conciliation. Conciliation is when a benevolent third party or government representative, when a labor-capital dispute is about to occur or has already occurred, acts as an intermediary to bring the two parties closer to each other and reach a collective agreement. Conciliation can be divided into two types:

A. Preventive Conciliation. The significance of preventive conciliation is that when a labor-capital dispute is brewing, the feelings of both labor and capital are approaching a breaking point, and the behavior of labor and capital conflict has not yet manifested. At this time, a second party who knows that both labor and capital hold firm opinions and will eventually conflict, comes forward to act as an intermediary for benevolent conciliation, so that both parties make concessions to eliminate the disaster in the invisible. According to this type of conciliation, it is easy to start and easy to succeed before the feelings of both parties are damaged, which is called preventive conciliation.

B. Ex Post Conciliation. Ex post conciliation refers to the fact that labor and capital have already had a dispute. After a labor dispute occurs, the situation is serious. On one side, a strike is declared or a riot is premeditated, and on the other side, the power of the military and police is used to prepare for suppression. A bloody tragedy is inevitable. At this time, a third party, unwilling to see the vicious fighting between labor and capital affecting social security, comes forward to invite the parties concerned to a meeting to resolve the difficulties. However, ex post conciliation can be divided into arbitrary conciliation and compulsory conciliation:

a. Arbitrary Conciliation. Whether or not labor and capital are willing to accept conciliation is up to the decision of both parties and has no binding force. If either party of labor and capital is unwilling to accept conciliation, then the effectiveness of conciliation is immediately lost. In arbitrary conciliation, there are so-called passive conciliation and active conciliation. In passive conciliation, even if the conciliation mechanism has been organized, whether both parties are willing to use it is up to the convenience of both parties concerned. For example, the French conciliation regulations of 1892 are so stipulated. As for active conciliation, local officials are responsible for advising both parties to adhere to the principle of peace and not insist on their own opinions. However, they have no power to force both parties to accept.

b. Compulsory Conciliation. Compulsory conciliation is different from arbitrary conciliation. After government representatives and local officials act as conciliators, both parties must accommodate the conciliation opinions, otherwise the state will come out and enforce them compulsorily. For example, the conciliation regulations of Sweden, etc., are so stipulated.

(2) Investigation. The meaning of investigation is that government agencies or investigation courts conduct thorough investigations of labor-capital disputes and officially announce various facts to the public, so that the public can understand the truth of the dispute and have concrete and powerful public opinion. If public opinion is dissatisfied with labor or capital, it will make labor or capital aware of their own mistakes, voluntarily withdraw the dispute, and return to peace. This is the so-called reference to social sanctions to eliminate social disputes. However, the effectiveness of the investigation system is extremely small, so in fact, fewer people adopt it.

(3) Arbitration. Arbitration has the nature of a public judgment. Because the above two methods are not easy to be effective, countries have established arbitration mechanisms to deal with labor-capital disputes. But in practice, countries start with conciliation first. If conciliation fails, it is immediately followed by arbitration. Therefore, the arbitration mechanism is nothing less than the highest court for labor-capital reconciliation. Arbitration can also be divided into arbitrary arbitration and compulsory arbitration. Arbitrary arbitration is only possible with the consent of both labor and capital. Furthermore, the result of the judgment has no power to force both parties to comply. Therefore, arbitrary arbitration is not as effective as compulsory arbitration. This is because compulsory arbitration is based on the laws promulgated by the state. Once a judgment is made, both parties must abide by it, otherwise severe penalties will be imposed.

V. Changes in China's Labor-Capital Dispute Handling Law. According to the first Labor-Capital Dispute Handling Law promulgated by the National Government in 1928, China adopted a compulsory arbitration system. In March 1930, the Legislative Yuan amended it and changed it to arbitrary arbitration. However, after it was changed to arbitrary arbitration, the arbitration ruling lacked compulsory force in law and could not bind both labor and capital to accept the ruling. Therefore, after the January 28th Shanghai War, the labor unrest in Shanghai was surging. Due to the relationship of arbitrary arbitration, labor-capital disputes were not easily resolved for a time, and society was greatly affected. For example, the labor-capital dispute of the Sanyou Industrial Company dragged on for years, from conciliation to arbitration, and from arbitration to court litigation, which was delayed and unresolved, and both parties suffered great losses. Wu Tiecheng, the mayor of Shanghai, realized this and proposed to the Central Political Conference to restore compulsory arbitration. Later, the Legislative Yuan revised the Labor-Capital Dispute Handling Law and restored the former compulsory arbitration system. Therefore, China's laws on labor-capital disputes have been changed repeatedly, but based on factual relations, it is felt that compulsory arbitration is actually more effective than arbitrary arbitration.

As for the main points of compulsory arbitration, it can be divided into five: (1) Labor-capital disputes must be submitted to arbitration after conciliation has no results. (2) Witnesses must testify and submit witness statements. (3) Lockouts and strikes are prohibited when conciliation evidence is being reviewed and judgments are being made. (4) Arbitration must be ruled and announced. (5) The ruling must be enforced and no objection may be raised. Lockouts and strikes are prohibited during the effective period, and violators will be fined or imprisoned.

Since the restoration of the compulsory arbitration system, labor-capital disputes in Shanghai have indeed decreased compared to before. From this, it can be seen that the effectiveness of compulsory arbitration is actually greater than that of arbitrary arbitration. The author personally advocated that the government adopt compulsory arbitration in the past because the government can exercise its control power to eliminate labor-capital disputes in the invisible.

VI. Italy's Labor-Capital Dispute Handling Law. Among the labor-capital dispute handling laws of various countries, Italy's law is the most stringent. Strikes and lockouts are all prohibited. All labor-capital disputes are resolved by the labor court's legal decision. After its implementation, the effect is remarkable and the results are excellent. It is specially introduced below for reference by the Chinese people and as the end of this article.

The law promulgated by the Italian government on April 3, 1926, stipulates that if a factory is closed without reason to force workers to accept conditions lower than those stipulated in the collective agreement, the government will fine the employer 10,000 to 100,000 lire. At the same time, if a strike is used to seek conditions higher than those stipulated in the contract, the government will also fine the workers 100 to 1,000 lire. In addition to paying the fine, strike leaders must also be imprisoned for one or two years. Furthermore, the Italian government's definition of a strike is very strict. Any cessation of work by more than three people requesting employers to provide treatment beyond the contract is considered a strike.

Workers in public agencies, such as postal and telecommunications workers, who strike without reason should be imprisoned for one or six months and suspended from work for six months. Strike leaders should be imprisoned for six months or two years and suspended from work for more than three years. As for employers of a public utility nature, if they close a factory without reason, they should pay a fine of 9,000 to 100,000 lire and be imprisoned for six months or one year.

The Italian government not only prohibits economic strikes but also prohibits political strikes. Because political strikes are sufficient to damage the government's prestige. Therefore, the penalties for those who participate in this type of strike are even more severe. It is stipulated that all those who participate in a strike should be imprisoned for one or three years. Those who instigate this type of strike should be imprisoned for three or seven years and permanently deprived of the right to work.

Page 7

Local News

The New Currency Policy is Effective, Increasing Funds and Revitalizing the Market; Three Banks Handle Overdrafts, All Banks and Firms Accept Mortgages; Banks Prepare for Year-End Closing, Temporarily Tightening Lending 94

After the implementation of the Ministry of Finance's new currency policy, it has yielded considerable results. Three banks handle interbank overdrafts, and silver firms accept mortgages in accordance with regulations. The increase in funds in the market has gradually revitalized it. As the year-end bank closing approaches, all lending is temporarily tightened. The market interest rate for foreign exchange has fallen. Details are as follows:

Handling Overdrafts and Accepting Mortgages

After the Central Bank of China, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications received an order from the Ministry of Finance to handle interbank overdrafts, the total amount is determined at any time depending on the market, allocated according to a 4-4-2 ratio, and managed by the Central Bank's Business Bureau according to established practice. Silver firms that have business relations with the three banks can apply for overdrafts. The Silver Firms Association, upon receiving an order from the Ministry of Finance to accept mortgages from various firms in accordance with regulations, has instructed its members to comply. Now, all banks and silver firms have complied with the ministry's order.

New Policies Take Effect, Market Revitalizes

The Ministry of Finance's new currency policy has been quite effective. The increase in funds in the market alleviates concerns about shortages. At the same time, the Central Bank of China, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications are handling interbank overdrafts, and the Shanghai Industry and Commerce Loan Examination Committee is handling industrial and commercial credit loans. Various industries are promoting commercial acceptance drafts, thus gradually revitalizing the market. The daily announced interest rate for foreign exchange in the silver market, such as today's drop to eight percent, sufficiently proves that the money supply in Shanghai has eased.

Bank Closing, Lending Tightens

As the year-end bank closing for the Republic of China's 24th year is approaching, the Bankers Association has scheduled its 9th Members' General Assembly to report on association affairs at 4:00 PM on the 28th. Banks are very busy preparing for the year-end closing. All new loans will be temporarily tightened during this closing period and will be reviewed and released after the closing. According to reporters from Xin Sheng She who inquired in banking circles, despite the economic depression, member banks of the Bankers Association are expected to still make a profit this year.

Silver Firms to Discuss Year-End Closing

The year-end closing for the Republic of China's 24th year in Shanghai's various industries has always been based on the silver industry. The Silver Firms Association will submit the issue of the year-end closing period to the next members' representatives meeting for discussion and decision. At the same time, it will also discuss all preparations before the year-end closing. It is reported that various silver firms are also temporarily tightening credit lending as the year-end closing approaches. Various industries are also preparing for this year's year-end closing, all hoping to overcome this difficulty, which is even more serious than the closing at the end of April and October.

Beijing-Shanghai, Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways Change Train Schedules; Effective December 21st; Highlights of the Newly Revised Train Schedule 98

The train schedules for the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways have been in effect since they were revised on July 1st of last year and have been in use for over a year. In May of this year, the Ministry of Railways convened the 9th National Railway Transportation Conference, which resolved to improve the speed of passenger and freight trains on various lines, shorten schedules, and increase transportation efficiency. The two railway administrations were ordered to draft specific proposals for review. The vehicle and machine departments jointly consulted and, based on the principle of increasing speed and reducing the number of stops, made improvements and drafted new passenger and freight train schedules for the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou lines. The existing schedules for the Shanghai-Xiang section and the Shanghai-Song section of the Beijing-Shanghai Railway are still able to meet current needs and have not been changed. On the Cao-Ning section, only train No. 254 is advanced by five minutes from Ningbo Station, and train No. 257 is advanced by five minutes from Yuyao Station; the rest remains the same. Regarding the Shanghai-Ping through train, the Ministry ordered consultation with representatives of the Tianjin-Pukou and Beining Railways to change the train schedule. However, since the time saved after the change was limited, and the Ministry's principle of handing over cars on the south bank could not be maintained, and there were conflicts with the connection times of the Jiaoji and Longhai Railways, it was agreed with the Tianjin-Pukou and Beining Railways to maintain the status quo. The new train schedule, the changes to passenger and freight trains, and the explanation of the reasons have now been submitted to the Ministry of Railways for approval and will be implemented from December 21st. The features of the newly revised schedule are disclosed as follows:

Increased Speed, Shortened Travel Time

(A) The first, second, third, and fourth express trains on the Beijing-Shanghai line originally required six hours and thirty minutes to six hours and forty-five minutes for the entire journey. Now, it only takes five hours and forty-five minutes to reach the destination, with the latest being five hours and fifty-five minutes, a reduction of more than half an hour compared to the current schedule. (B) The 21st and 22nd express trains on the Beijing-Shanghai line originally required nine hours and five minutes and nine hours for the entire journey. Now, it only takes eight hours and fifteen minutes and seven hours and forty minutes, a reduction of about one hour compared to the current schedule. (C) The 41st and 42nd slow trains of the third and fourth classes on the Beijing-Shanghai line, which are currently the 71st and 72nd slow trains of the third and fourth classes, originally required twelve hours and ten minutes and twelve hours and twenty-five minutes for the entire journey. Now, it only takes ten hours and fifty-five minutes and eleven hours and fifteen minutes, a reduction of more than one hour compared to the current schedule. (D) The first and second special express trains on the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo line originally required four hours and forty minutes and four hours and forty-five minutes. Now, it only takes four hours and fifteen minutes. The 11th and 12th special express trains originally required four hours and fifty-five minutes and five hours and five minutes. Now, it only takes four hours and thirty minutes and four hours and thirty-five minutes, a reduction of about half an hour compared to the current schedule. (E) The 21st, 32nd, 33rd, and 34th express trains on the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo line have also been reduced by about half an hour compared to the current schedule. In addition, the slow trains of the third and fourth classes have also been reduced by varying amounts.

Limiting the Number of Cars; The number of cars attached to each passenger train used to vary, and if the limit of the engine power was exceeded, it would easily lead to slow travel. Now, the number is strictly limited according to the engine capacity to reduce delays.

Reducing the Number of Stops; Special express trains and express trains take at least five or six minutes to stop at each station. Now, the first, second, and fourth trains on the Beijing-Shanghai line will cancel stops at Kunshan Station, the 21st train will cancel stops at Shizi, Xinfeng, Xinzha Town, and Shitangwan stations, and the 22nd train will cancel stops at Guandu Li, Xin 高资, Xia Shu, Lou Shan, and five stations. The 12th express train on the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo line will cancel stops at Fengjing Station, the 31st and 32nd trains will cancel stops at Xujiahui Station, and the 33rd train will cancel stops at Xieqiao and Linping stations to shorten travel time and reduce the boredom of long-distance travelers.

Adding Intercity Express and Express Trains; (A) After the Shanghai-Ping through train departs from the North Shanghai Station at 4:00 PM, there are no express or special express trains available on the Beijing-Shanghai line. Now, the current 78th Shanghai-Changzhou mixed third and fourth class intercity train will be changed to the 24th Shanghai-Changzhou special express intercity train, departing from Shanghai at 4:50 PM and arriving at Suzhou Station at 6:43 PM, Wuxi Station at 7:37 PM, and Changzhou Station at 8:35 PM. The travel time is shortened by one hour and twenty-two minutes to two hours and thirty minutes compared to the current schedule. Passengers within the Changzhou-Shanghai section can return home earlier and have ample time to stay in Shanghai. (B) The current 77th Changzhou-Shanghai second, third, and fourth class mixed intercity train on the Beijing-Shanghai line departs from Changzhou too early. There are no express or special trains available in the Shanghai-Changzhou section in the morning. Now, the departure time from Changzhou will be delayed to 8:00 AM and changed to the 23rd express train.

Adjusting the Seats of the Third and Fourth Class Cars; The number of third and fourth class passengers on the Beijing-Shanghai line is greater in the afternoon than in the morning. The three trains departing first are overcrowded, and later arrivals have almost no room to stand, while the later trains have few passengers. Now, the current 73rd Changzhou-Shanghai second and fourth class mixed intercity train will be changed to the 45th Wuxi-Shanghai third and fourth class intercity train, departing from Wuxi to accommodate as many passengers as possible in the Wuxi-Shanghai section. The current 41st Beijing-Shanghai first and fourth class train will be changed to the 43rd Zhenjiang-Shanghai third and fourth class intercity train, departing from Zhenjiang West Station to accommodate as many passengers as possible in the Zhenjiang-Suzhou section. After passing Suzhou Station, the number of stops will be reduced as much as possible to shorten travel time and limit the number of passengers to alleviate congestion. Passengers in the Beijing-Zhenjiang section and late-arriving passengers at various stations along the way can take the last 41st train.

Adding a Midday Express Train to Beijing; There is currently no midday express train departing from Nanjing Station on the Beijing-Shanghai line. After the 21st express train departs at 9:30 AM, passengers must wait until 5:00 PM for the 3rd special express train. Now, the 21st express train will be delayed to 12:35 PM from Beijing.

Adjusting the Departure Time of Passenger Trains from the North Shanghai Station

The 22nd express train on the Beijing-Shanghai line currently departs from Shanghai at 9:00 AM, which is too close to the departure time of the 4th special express train. After the 22nd train departs, passengers must wait until 1:10 PM for the next special express train. Now, the 22nd express train will be delayed to 9:50 AM from Shanghai to adjust the departure time.

The Dutch Government is Cracking Down on Chinese People Going to Java 106

Passports and Deng Po Papers are Required to Purchase Tickets and Board Ships

Dutch shipping companies operating in the East Indies, the South Seas Islands, and Java have recently decided to reduce prices due to sluggish business and few passengers. In addition, the Dutch government is strictly cracking down on the entry of Chinese workers and has added restrictions on the sale of ship tickets. The details are as follows:

Passports Required for Java

In the past, Chinese people going to the South Seas Islands and ports such as Surabaya and Semarang in Dutch Java, such as laborers and workers, could enter the country by paying a head tax of 150 guilders and obtaining a Deng Po paper. Now, the Dutch authorities have strictly cracked down, and all those going to Java are considered as businessmen and tourists. The previously established practice of relying solely on Deng Po papers is no longer valid. The shipping companies traveling between China and Java are hereby notified that all Chinese people going to Java, regardless of whether they purchase tickets in Shanghai, Xiamen, or elsewhere, and regardless of whether they are new or old passengers, must apply for a Chinese passport. When purchasing ship tickets, they must first present their passport and Deng Po paper (commonly known as yellow paper). If either is missing, they may not purchase ship tickets. The local Zha Hua Shipping Company has complied with this new rule. Going to the South Seas will be very difficult for Chinese people in the future.

Dutch Ships to Discuss Ticket Price Reductions

The South Seas passenger ships of the Zha Hua Shipping Company also sail to Xiamen and Hong Kong. Shanghai passengers have always been crowded. This year, after China Merchants, Jardine Matheson, and others added new ships to the South China route, ticket prices were reduced, and the business of Dutch shipping has been slightly affected. The company has been discussing for days to reduce the ticket prices for each class on the Shanghai-Xiamen section to salvage the situation. As a result of the discussion, it is proposed that the first-class cabin from Shanghai to Xiamen be reduced from 85 yuan to 70 yuan, the second-class cabin from 60 yuan to 50 yuan, the third-class cabin from 35 yuan to 30 yuan, and the steerage cabin from 15 yuan to 12.5 yuan. For those going to Hong Kong, the first-class cabin is reduced from 110 yuan to 100 yuan, the second-class cabin from 60 yuan to 50 yuan, the third-class cabin from 35 yuan to 30 yuan, and the steerage cabin from 20 yuan to 17.5 yuan. These new ticket prices are scheduled to take effect from the next Vanikela.

Zhabei Charity Association Appeals to All Sectors for Funds to Establish Soup Kitchens 111

The Zhabei Charity Association of this city has issued a circular appealing to wealthy merchants and gentry in Shanghai for funds to urgently establish soup kitchens as winter approaches. The circular states: "Shanghai is a major commercial metropolis, and Zhabei is a factory district. The market is generally sluggish, and factories are bound to close. The working class faces extreme hardship. Every year during the harsh winter, the establishment of soup kitchens is eagerly anticipated by the poor. For the sake of stability, we cannot avoid establishing them. While we were raising funds, we received Instruction No. 11920 from the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, which stated that this year's floods in various provinces have been exceptionally severe, and the countryside is desolate. Countless impoverished victims of the disaster are fleeing to Shanghai. Coupled with the economic depression and the decline of all industries, it is difficult for the suffering people to obtain food and clothing. This year's situation is particularly dire, and it is even more necessary to establish soup kitchens. We are hereby ordered to begin preparations early." We are immediately complying and expediting preparations. In addition to requesting funds from the municipal government for promotion, we urgently appeal to the wealthy merchants and gentry of Shanghai, stating: "Soup kitchens fill stomachs. A single grain enters the belly. In the harsh winter, receiving a full meal in the early morning is invigorating and warming, not just filling the stomach. There is no greater virtue than this." We are currently constructing sheds and repairing pots at Beiliuying Road, and actively preparing. However, according to past practice, each factory serves over 10,000 people, requiring 30 to 40 piculs of rice per day. Based on a two-month budget, we need over 2,000 piculs of rice, totaling over 30,000 silver dollars. Our association has no permanent assets and relies entirely on the generous donations of benefactors. We will not send anyone out to solicit donations. Whether it is money, rice, or cotton clothing, any amount is welcome. Every grain of rice and drop of benevolence will be used for public benefit. In addition to sending out letters, we hereby respectfully inform you and humbly request your consideration." Respectfully, The Zhabei Charity Association Directors Yu Qiaqing, Wang Xiaolai, Du Yuesheng, Wen Lanting, Zhang Xiaolin, Jin Tingsun, Yuan Ludeng, Chen Bingqian, Xu Qianlin, Shen Lianfang, Lin Kanghou, Yu Yefeng, Wang Weiguan, Chen Weihan, Director Wang Binyan, and all board members jointly announce.

The Steamboat Trade Association of this city, in view of the recent increase in prices and the soaring costs of hardware, materials, machinery, and iron plates used by the steamboat industry due to foreign exchange rates, as well as the general increase in prices of daily necessities such as coal, which has led to huge expenses for steamboats, has decided at its 37th Executive Committee meeting to increase freight fares on all routes by 20% starting next month, in order to remedy the situation.

Shelter for the Destitute Prepared, Municipal Government Allocates 2,000 Yuan 113

Wang Yiting and Huang Hanzhi of the United Charity Association of this city, in order to provide relief to the hungry and cold common people of this city, and complying with the request of the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, are organizing temporary shelters for the destitute as usual. They have entrusted Director Zhang Zixin to negotiate with the board of directors of the Chaozhou Guild Hall at the South Railway Station and the Chao Hui Villa on Xietu Road to allocate the remaining houses for use. After days of arrangement and preparation, everything has been completed. However, the Chao Hui Villa is still occupied by the city's security team. They are currently looking for vacant houses elsewhere and will request the team to relocate as soon as they find one. The Association had previously reported the progress of preparations to the municipal government and requested an additional allocation of funds. Yesterday, they received an instruction stating: "Having reviewed the report, considering the strained financial situation of the city treasury, an allocation of 2,000 yuan is tentatively approved to meet the essential needs for operating the shelter for the destitute. The Finance Bureau is hereby instructed. Please take note of this order." The Association has prepared a letter and sent personnel to collect the funds in order to proceed with the operation. Yesterday's newspaper reported that the municipal government had approved a subsidy of over 11,000 yuan, which was actually raised by the Association from various charities. However, this year's floods in various provinces have been severe, leading to the bankruptcy of rural areas, economic depression, and an increasing number of unemployed people and impoverished citizens. At this time of severe cold, those suffering from cold and hunger are everywhere. It is expected that the number of people registering and requesting shelter will be even greater than in previous years. Final Instance: Wang Deyu Sentenced to Death, Judgment Rendered by Supreme Court 123

Murderer Wang Deyu (whose father's original surname was Ding, but he became an adopted son of the Wang family and his son Deyu took the Wang surname) is 28 years old, an ironworker, and from Wuxi. In the 22nd year [of the Republic, i.e. 1933], he plotted to seize his uncle's inheritance. On October 15th of that year, at noon, he lured his cousin Ding Fugen (13 years old, whose father's family-run Ding Juxing Iron Shop was located at 658 Xiaoshadu Road, West Shanghai. After his father's death, his mother, Ding Yin, continued to run the shop) from the front of the Sino-French School in Baxianqiao in the French Concession (Ding was a student at the school and boarded at his aunt's house on Laohe Road because of the inconvenient commute) to a cotton field in Yijiazhai of the Longhua Cement Factory, where he beat him to death with an iron implement. After the crime, Deyu fled without a trace. After investigation, the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau arrested a suspect named Zhou Ayuan from Jiangyin, who confessed that Wang was hiding in the Quanqui Inn in Nanxiang Town. Detectives rushed to the scene overnight and arrested Wang, who was brought to Shanghai for interrogation. Because the crime originated in the French Concession, the French police sent detectives to the Public Security Bureau to take back the two suspects, Wang and Zhou, and send them to the Second Special District Court. The French Police Department filed a public prosecution for premeditated murder. The initial trial sentenced Wang Deyu to death for premeditated murder, and deprived him of civil rights for life. Zhou Ayuan was found not guilty. Later, Zhou was released after the Police Department did not appeal. However, Wang refused to accept the death sentence and appealed to the Third High Court, hoping to evade punishment and blaming his brother-in-law Tang Aming for the murder of Ding Fugen. After repeated court hearings, the High Court found that Wang's grounds for appeal were empty and unfounded, and the evidence of the crime was solid. The court rejected his appeal. Wang still refused to accept the sentence and filed a third appeal to the Supreme Court. The suspect is still being held in the detention center of the Second Special District Court. It has now been learned that the Supreme Court has reviewed the entire case file and still believes that Wang's crime is certain. The court has ruled in the case of Wang Deyu's appeal against the murder conviction, stating: "The original judgment is reversed regarding the criminal sentence. Wang Deyu is sentenced to death for murder and deprived of civil rights for life." This judgment will be executed in accordance with the law after approval by the Ministry of Justice.

Liu Zirong, the third and youngest son of Liu Huizhi, the former general manager of the China Industrial Bank, married Xi Yunqing (also known as Yunqing), the daughter of the paint tycoon Xi Ehan.
