A Murderous Drama Over a One Copper Coin Dispute Inside a Restaurant 125

Wei Xunchen, a cloth merchant from Anhui residing at the back street of the Nanshi Artillery Factory, 25 years old, went to the Shengho Restaurant at 116 Xixinqiao Street in the French Concession, run by Yang Baochu from Wuxi, for lunch at noon on the 7th of this month with a friend. After the meal, the total cost of the food was over 600 cash. Wei handed over a double mill and several copper coins to pay the bill. The restaurant's cashier valued the double mill at 520 cash. Wei argued that the exchange rate at the tobacco and paper shops outside was 530 cash, and it should be accepted at the prevailing market rate, and he should not be shortchanged one copper coin. The cashier then ordered Wei to go outside and exchange the money. However, Wei took the double mill outside and did not exchange it, nor did he return to the restaurant to pay the bill. He went forward. The restaurant waiter saw him and caught up with him, stopping Wei and bringing him back to the restaurant. The two sides started arguing. At that time, two of Wei's fellow villagers, Liang Maotou and Li Zhongfu, were also eating at the Shengho Restaurant. Hearing the commotion, they came out to help Wei commit the violence, twisting and beating the waiter. The patrol officer saw this and brought both parties into the police station for investigation. Suddenly, several hooligans from Anhui heard about the matter and rushed to the Shengho Restaurant to make trouble, destroying a large number of bowls, pots, and other items. At that time, Wei Xunchen, also from Anhui, was stabbed by Yang Xipei, a waiter from Wuxi, with a knife, causing him to bleed profusely. For a time, passersby watched a martial drama erupting over a dispute of one copper coin. Xu tried to intervene, and the French police, hearing the news, immediately dispatched a large number of detectives in patrol cars to suppress the situation, disperse the idlers, and arrest the assailants Yang Xipei and the Anhui people Li Shuxin, Li Zhenglun, and Li Yunze, who were fighting at the scene, and took them to the police station for detention. Yesterday, they were sent to the Eighth Criminal Court of the Second Special District Court, where Judge Sun Pengxian conducted a preliminary hearing. The police department's lawyer stated that the police station needed to arrest the criminals to conduct a detailed investigation and requested a postponement. The court approved the request after briefly questioning the defendants and ordered that the defendants be remanded in custody.

Grand Opening Ceremony of the Shan Juan Cave 127

All Lanterns Lit Starting From the 10th of This Month - Day Trip Possible Via the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway

The secluded, deep, peculiar, and magnificent Shan Juan and Geng Sang Caves in Yixing have long been renowned both domestically and internationally. Since the opening of the highway, transportation has become convenient, and the number of visitors has increased daily, thus enhancing the fame of the two caves. According to reliable sources, the entire renovation project of the Shan Juan Cave has now been completed, and the grand opening ceremony is scheduled to take place on the 10th of this month. The original upper, middle, and lower three levels have been connected into one, and all lanterns have been lit, allowing visitors to explore its depths without the trouble of groping in the dark. It is also reported that the cave will be permanently open to the public after its opening. Electrical Expert Sun Qi Invents the "Electric Hot Water Bottle" 134

As winter approaches, the old-fashioned practice of using foot stoves to warm bedding is inherently dangerous. Even the more modern hot water bottles have the inconvenience of frequent water filling and emptying, as well as the potential for leaks and repairs. Recently, electrical expert Mr. Sun Qi, based on his years of research, has invented an "electric hot water bottle." Each night, after a single five-minute electrical charge, it can keep the bed warm all night. The procedure is simple, clean, and safe. The style is attractive, the cost is low, and in addition to providing warmth, it can also be used as an iron. It is truly an extremely economical household item. Mr. Sun is currently applying for a patent and is seeking cooperation with electrical appliance manufacturers to enable mass production and sales. Mr. Sun works in the capital. If electrical appliance manufacturers wish to inquire, they can contact Sun Zhenqiu at the Jiufeng Flour Mill at the Railway Bridge, Xiaguan, Nanjing.

Young Men Hire Car, Leaving Behind Cloth Banner and Handguns - Suspicious Actions of Three Men, Secrecy Surrounding Banner Slogans 135

Yesterday morning around 9:00 AM, a taxi company, Xinghua, located at 5 Dongyouheng Road, reported that three passengers had hired a car and, upon completion of the ride, left a rolled-up cloth banner and a square paper box containing two handguns in the car. The incident was discovered by the taxi driver, who reported it to the accounting office, which then reported it to the Hongkou Police Station. A strict investigation is currently underway. Details are as follows:

Young Men Hire Car

The Xinghua Taxi Company, located at 5 Dongyouheng Road, Hongkou, has been operating for years. At 9:15 yesterday morning, a well-dressed young man, claiming to be surnamed Song and around 30 years old, approached the company's accounting office and stated that he needed to hire a car to go to the French Concession and the Bund to pick up relatives and friends.

Stopped at Alley Entrance

The company's accounting office immediately completed the rental form and handed it to the on-duty taxi driver, Xu Guilin, who drove a taxi with license plate number Zujie 17694 (Huajie 4465). The customer calmly boarded the car, and the taxi sped towards the French Concession. When the car reached the intersection of Fuli Road and Fukaissen Road, the customer ordered the driver to stop the car near an alley entrance.

Cloth Banner and Gift Present

As soon as the car stopped, two men were already waiting at the alley entrance. One of them held a rolled-up cloth banner, and the other carried a square paper box, about a foot in size, resembling a gold-lettered gift present. The two men successively boarded the car, and the three men sat side by side. They then ordered the driver to drive the car to the intersection of Wuma Road and Sichuan Road. Upon reaching the intersection, the two men who had boarded the car later got out empty-handed, leaving the cloth banner and paper box inside the car.

Entered Customs House

At this time, only the young man who had hired the car remained inside. After the two men got out, the young man ordered the driver to drive the car to the Bund, outside the customs house. The driver obeyed and drove. Soon, the car arrived at the back entrance of the customs house on the Bund and stopped. After getting out of the car, the young man hastily took out two yuan from his pocket and paid the driver, and then hurriedly walked into the back entrance of the customs house. The driver immediately drove the empty car back to the company.

Heavy Square Box

When taxi driver Xu Guilin returned to the company, he happened to glance back and suddenly discovered a rolled-up banner and a paper box, realizing that they had been left behind by the two passengers who boarded the car later. Thinking that the customers had forgotten them due to an urgent matter, he intended to take them to the accounting office for safekeeping, waiting for the customers to claim them. However, as soon as he picked up the square box, he felt that it was quite heavy. So he handed the banner and box to the accounting office together.

Two Handguns

The accounting office took the banner and box, and according to routine, had to check the contents of the box to avoid errors. When the paper cover was opened, two live handguns were clearly revealed. At that time, the company staff all expressed shock, and for the sake of caution, they immediately reported the incident to the Hongkou Police Station. The police chief immediately dispatched Chinese and Western detectives to investigate.

Police Secret Investigation

The police first questioned taxi driver Xu Guilin in detail, and then took Xu to the taxi stand and the places where the two passengers boarded and alighted, where Xu gave separate accounts of the situation at that time. Finally, they went to the customs house and inquired extensively, but there was no trace of the young man who had hired the car. However, the fact that the three men had secretly transported two handguns to that place raised suspicions about their intentions. The police are currently conducting a strict investigation. As for the type of slogans written on the abandoned rolled-up banner, the police are keeping it a secret and it is not convenient to disclose.

Arrest of Person Mixing Old Silver Dollars in Central Bank - Guangdong Elderly Woman Exchanging Old Silver for Legal Tender - Wang Wanchun Impersonates Bank Employee to Accept Exchange 137

-Suspect Discovered and Arrested by Central Bank-

Since the Ministry of Finance issued an order prohibiting the use of old silver dollars, the Central Bank in this city established a special office to collect old silver and exchange it for legal tender. Recently, the bank has been experiencing incidents of people mixing in to exchange old silver, so they have been paying close attention. At 11:00 AM on the 7th of this month, Ms. Li Ye, an elderly woman from Guangdong, brought twenty old silver dollars to the bank's exchange office to exchange for legal tender. Wang Wanchun, a Jiangbei native who lives at 33 Huazhen Lane, Xinjiang Road, Zhabei, and makes a living by renting out rickshaws, stepped forward and claimed to be an employee of the Central Bank. He said that he could exchange the silver dollars for her, and it would be the same, and he could exchange them immediately. Ms. Li believed him and handed him the silver dollars. Wang then gave her twenty yuan in banknotes. This was seen by Xia Erchang, an employee of the bank, who reported it to Lin Shiliang, the director of the administration department. Sun Jishen, a Chinese detective, and Chinese constable number 3389 arrived and arrested Wang and took him into custody at the General Police Station. Ms. Li Ye then testified that the defendant exchanged the money with her at the time, and she handed him the silver dollars, and he gave her banknotes, but she was afraid that they were counterfeit, so she returned them. Emergency Meeting of Rickshaw Guild and Penalized Rickshaw Owners 138

360 Licenses Confiscated This Month - Joint Request to Taxpayers Association to Negotiate with Public Works Department

Xin Sheng News Agency reports that the Special District Rickshaw Owners Guild, due to the Rickshaw Committee's abuse of power in confiscating licenses and imposing arbitrary fines, convened an emergency meeting of penalized rickshaw owners yesterday morning. More than 50 people attended, chaired by Jin Chunlin. He reported that 136 licenses had been confiscated in November, and 360 licenses have been confiscated this month. Each license carries a fine of ten yuan. Although representatives have been sent to negotiate, there has been no concrete solution. After discussion, it was resolved that: (1) If the Rickshaw Committee does not provide a satisfactory response by the 10th of this month, another meeting will be held at 9:00 AM on the 11th to discuss measures to sanction Zhu Maocheng for abusing his authority and arbitrarily punishing rickshaw owners. (2) All penalized rickshaw owners will jointly write to the Taxpayers Association, requesting them to negotiate with the Public Works Department. (3) Refuse to accept the unreasonable penalties of the Rickshaw Committee (because rickshaw owners only collect four small silver coins and eight copper coins per shift, which complies with the regulations of collecting eight jiao and five fen of silver dollars per day and does not overcharge rent). The Guild also presented a document to the Taxpayers Association stating: The petition is regarding the abuse of power and the daily occurrence of license confiscation and fines, requesting assistance to stop the oppression. Our Guild's rickshaw owners in the Special District, since the Public Works Department's Rickshaw Committee proposed rent reductions last spring, after much debate by the rickshaw owners, the Public Works Department convened an equal meeting between rickshaw owner representatives and the Rickshaw Committee on August 6 of the same year. As a result of the discussions, it was agreed that the total rent, including the driver's mutual aid fund fee, should be eight jiao and five fen of silver dollars per day. Later, because the rickshaw pullers did not have silver dollars to pay the rent, both parties reconsidered and changed to twelve jiao of small silver coins. The facts are available for verification. Until November of this year, when the new currency system was implemented, the Rickshaw Committee published a notice on the 9th of the same month, also sending a letter to our Guild's Special District office, stating that the rent collected should not exceed eight jiao and five fen of silver dollars, and that if it is small silver coins, each shift can only collect five jiao and three copper coins, and two shifts a day should only collect ten jiao and six copper coins. Our office immediately forwarded the letter to all rickshaw owners and asked them to inform the licensees to comply. Unexpectedly, before the letter was even disseminated, the Rickshaw Committee, based on the inaccurate reports of rickshaw pullers, believed that the rickshaw owners were overcharging rent and abusing their powers, and began confiscating licenses and imposing fines on a daily basis. For example, a fine of ten yuan is required for one confiscated license, and a fine of one hundred yuan is required for ten confiscated licenses, and so on. If the fines are not paid, the licenses will be confiscated. The misunderstandings in the penalties imposed within a month are numerous. To briefly explain, the rickshaws are rented out in two shifts, morning and evening. However, the operating hours are different for each rickshaw line. If the morning and evening shifts are equal, the rent will naturally be the same. If the morning shift is short and the evening shift is long, the rent will naturally vary. The current misunderstanding is that the morning shift collects four jiao and six fen of small silver coins, and the evening shift collects six jiao of small silver coins. The Rickshaw Committee only listens to the evening shift drivers and does not investigate the morning shift rental price, which is the first reason. In addition, the Rickshaw Committee allows rickshaw owners or licensees to collect rickshaw pullers' loans, unpaid rent, and housing fees, according to the document exchanged on November 30 of last year. The reason for this misunderstanding is that many rickshaw owners or licensees collected the above-mentioned items, which caused dissatisfaction among the rickshaw pullers, who reported the matter summarily. The Rickshaw Committee did not distinguish or assess the situation and simply ruled that the rent had been overcharged, which is the second reason. Although the rickshaw owners explained and debated repeatedly, the Rickshaw Committee ignored them and said that those who applied for reconsideration would be doubly punished if summoned a second time, regardless of whether the charges were true or not. There were also cases where, if summoned during a period of time and were unable to attend due to circumstances, they would be doubly punished once summoned. "For example, if the original fine was ten yuan per vehicle, the rickshaw owner would have to pay two hundred yuan if the rickshaw owner has the above two situations." Not only are the penalties unwarranted, but they are also aggravated. The Western and Chinese members of the committee, such as Gao Bi, wield their power and their words are law, leaving little room for discussion, which is alarming. The rickshaw owners, oppressed and devastated by this, have come to the Guild to report the situation, full of indignation and anger, with tears in their eyes. Previously, our office sent a letter to the Rickshaw Committee, requesting it to carefully consider the situation and handle it with leniency. The rickshaw owners should correct their faults if they have any, and encourage themselves if they don't have any. After the letter was sent, the committee replied that it would still act arbitrarily and not adopt the suggestions. On December 2, the committee convened a general meeting of all rickshaw owners in the Special District and publicly elected representatives such as Yin Zhiling and Hou Shaoan to negotiate. As a result, the committee said that whether or not to implement the penalties would be decided by the Board of Directors on the 10th of this month. The representatives thought that there was a possibility of change, but since then, the number of rickshaw owners summoned for penalties has increased day by day, which is even more shocking. We believe that every rickshaw owner in the Special District is aware of the situation. Under the pressure of being repeatedly fined, they would still dare to overcharge a small amount of rent, risking large fines or the confiscation of their licenses for a month. Even foolish rickshaw owners would not be so foolish. The reason is that the rickshaw pullers and rickshaw owners inevitably have grievances at times. Now, because the Rickshaw Committee suppresses the rickshaw owners and favors the rickshaw pullers, they will summon and punish them regardless of the truth. Therefore, the rickshaw pullers dare to take this opportunity to retaliate, which is why the number of cases is increasing. (It has been found that more than 50 rickshaw owners and licensees have been fined and had their licenses confiscated, involving about 500 rickshaws. A separate form is attached.) If this continues, the impact will be great, and disputes will be numerous. The public rickshaw industry is on the verge of bankruptcy. Your Guild is the only legal organization of Chinese taxpayers, dedicated to promoting the welfare of citizens and supporting various industries, which is universally admired. Therefore, we are submitting this request, hoping that you will consider the situation, speak out for justice, and forward this letter to the Public Works Department, requesting them to stop the Rickshaw Committee from abusing its powers and to exempt all the fines and confiscations, so that the rickshaw owners will not suffer endless losses and the escalating disputes can be resolved. Our industry will be fortunate, and society will be fortunate. We are anxiously awaiting your response.

Relieve the Burden on Tenants - Prosper the Whole Society

Da Gong News Agency reports that the Municipal Rent Reduction Committee believes that the rent reduction issue has been repeatedly requested from the authorities to set a standard, but for various reasons, it has not been promulgated. The reason for this is that rent expenses account for 50-60% of daily expenses. Therefore, the once-prosperous Shanghai is now lined with empty houses, with no one asking about them, and the unemployed population is increasing daily. Our committee is horrified by the prospects. It is a last resort, and we hope you will understand. As for the disputes that have already occurred, our committee will send personnel to mediate. In addition, please announce a voluntary rent reduction for the houses that have not yet reduced rents. It is related to the whole society, and we hope you will adopt our suggestion. We will be very grateful for your cooperation."

Business Printing Press to Implement Acceptance Drafts Starting Today 141

The Business Printing Press of this city is the largest cultural organization in the country. It deals with no fewer than four hundred factories and businesses on a daily basis for printing and manufacturing, as well as procuring raw materials. For the convenience of clients in collecting accounts, it is stipulated that payments be made on the 15th and 31st of each month. The press also notifies clients of the amounts due in advance by postcard, allowing them to pay on time. Therefore, clients invariably consider it convenient. However, in recent years, various industries have been sluggish, and financing has been extremely tight. The press, in order to further assist its partner factories and businesses with capital turnover, has decided to adopt commercial acceptance drafts starting today. The following are the press's provisional measures: for any delivery worth more than 100 national currency units, the client may issue an application to have half of the amount accepted in advance, while the remaining half will be paid in accordance with the original payment method. As for clients who wish to cash or discount the drafts at a bank, they are generally required to provide a guarantor. However, this procedure presents difficulties for small factories. Therefore, the press has specifically consulted with the Hongkou branch of the Bank of China, the Jiangxi Road branch of the Jin Cheng Bank, and the Ningbo Road branch of the Shanghai Bank. Small factories with no prior dealings with banks may, with the press's prior approval, deposit their seals with the aforementioned banks, so that they can cash or discount the drafts based on the seals and interest rates. The aforementioned three banks, in order to support domestic industry and commerce, have also generally agreed to provide special preferential treatment. Due to the various conveniences mentioned above, partner factories and shops have been enthusiastically contacting the press to adopt this system. It is said that the press will have to increase its procedural workload by one-third in order to automatically adopt acceptance drafts in addition to the original payment method, but for the sake of facilitating the turnover of funds for its clients, it is still determined to implement the system.

Suiyuan Missionary Society Plans to Purchase 30,000 Copies of Wang Yunwu's Concise Dictionary Arranged According to the Four-Corner Method 142

The Four-Corner Number Indexing Method invented by Mr. Wang Yunwu can be mastered by scholars in two hours. Each character can be found in an average of only 8.9 seconds. It is easy to learn and easy to use, breaking the records of other indexing methods. Many party and government agencies, academic organizations, libraries, and schools in China have adopted it. American libraries and Japanese publications have also occasionally adopted this method. Many other dictionaries, encyclopedias, and large books also include Four-Corner Number Indexes. Scholars can find what they need quickly and easily when consulting these books. Recently, the call for eliminating illiteracy has grown louder, and educational administrative agencies in various places have spared no effort in promoting compulsory education. Tibetan Lama Song Kanbu's Theft Case Settled 143

Criminal Suit That Cannot Be Withdrawn Concluded by the Court Yesterday

Tibetan Lama Song Kanbu of the Sera Monastery came to Nanjing to attend the Sixth Plenary Session of the Kuomintang Central Executive Committee. After the meeting ended on the 30th of last month, he came to Shanghai and stayed in Room 257 of the Andong Hotel on Hubei Road. He then discovered that all the cash and silver dollars totaling 300 yuan and 13 taels of saffron in his suitcase had disappeared. Suspecting that the hotel was involved in the theft, he filed a lawsuit with the First Special District Court. The hotel responded through its accountant, Yao Yunfang, who filed counterclaims of false accusation and defamation. This matter has been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Dai Rongduo continued the hearing in Criminal Court No. 9. The case has now been mediated by Jiang Ganting, president of the World Red Swastika Society. Because Song's travel expenses had been completely stolen, preventing him from returning to Tibet, Jiang persuaded the Andong Hotel to subsidize him with 100 silver dollars and the Red Swastika Society to subsidize him with 150 silver dollars to cover his travel expenses. This mediation plan was accepted by both parties, so the private suit was settled and withdrawn by Song. As for Andong's counterclaim of defamation, it was subject to prosecution and was also withdrawn. The remaining original suit and counterclaim of false accusation could not be withdrawn according to law, and Judge Dai proceeded with the trial. He summoned the hotel's tea server, receptionist, and others to court for detailed questioning. Then, he ordered the start of the debate, with the plaintiff's lawyer, Dong Yu, and the defendant's lawyer, Wang Chuanbi, arguing back and forth. Judge Dai then announced the end of the debate and scheduled a date for sentencing.

Authentic Drafts of Bai Shi Qiao Published, Tales Under the Bean Arbor Released at the Same Time 150

Chen Meigong of Yun Jian was a great Confucian scholar of the Ming Dynasty. He lamented the changes in the world and lived in seclusion, refusing to serve as an official. His poems and essays were famous throughout the country. During the late Ming Dynasty, there was a trend among men of letters to compete in publishing books. Chen Meigong compiled and authored many books. He once compiled and published Bao Yan Tang Secret Manuscripts, which was a major collection of essays of the Ming Dynasty. His own writings included the Ten Kinds of Chen Meigong Series, of which Authentic Drafts of Bai Shi Qiao is one. The entire book contains 24 volumes, written in a fragrant and lively style, and is a model of essays. There are also 24 volumes of Essays from the Late Fragrance Hall, which were compiled by his disciples. If these are published together, they can be called the Complete Works of Chen Meigong. The fourteenth title in the Rare Chinese Literature Series is carefully collated by A Ying, with a postscript by Shi Zhecun and a cover inscription by Lu Jiye. It is divided into two volumes, containing over 400 pages and over 300,000 words. The retail price for the entire set is only 60 cents, and the special edition is 90 cents. In addition, the thirteenth title, the critical short story Tales Under the Bean Arbor, is a superb work of short fiction from the early Qing Dynasty. Zheng Zhenduo highly praised it in his Essays on Literature. It has now been carefully collated by Dai Wangshu, with a cover inscription by Hu Shi. The retail price has been drastically reduced to make it widely accessible, with the regular edition priced at only 20 cents and the special edition at only 25 cents. The poetry and essay collection of Yuan Bosiu, the founder of the Gong'an School of the Ming Dynasty, was published last week. The collection, White Su Zhai, was compiled by his younger brothers, Yuan Zhonglang and Yuan Xiaoxiu, and is superior to any other edition. To understand the origins of the New Literature Movement, one must trace it back to Gong'an and Jingling. Those who wish to study the writings of the Gong'an School cannot afford to overlook this collection of Yuan Bosiu's essays. There are two types of retail prices: 40 cents and 50 cents. The entire collection of 50 titles in the Rare Book Series can be pre-ordered for a total of 17 yuan, which is only equivalent to the price of one woodblock-printed book. General Distributor: Shanghai Magazine Company, No. 324 Sima Road.

Education News

Director of Social Education Department Zhang Jiong Discusses Implementation of Simplified Characters in July of Next Year 154

(Nanjing, 9th Dispatch) Zhang Jiong, Director of the Social Education Department of the Ministry of Education, stated that the implementation of simplified characters is scheduled for July of next year. Regarding the casting of character fonts, the Ministry has commissioned the Shanghai Zhonghua Book Company to cast phonetic typefaces, and five sets have now been completed. The number of simplified character fonts being cast by the Shanghai Zhonghua Book Company is dependent on demand. In the future, they will be distributed to various publishing houses for use at the original casting cost. When the time comes, if primary school textbooks and children's reading materials in various bookstores do not adopt the simplified characters promulgated by the Ministry, the Ministry of Education will not approve them and will suspend their sales.

Ministry of Education Commissioners for Compulsory Education Set Off 155

(Nanjing, 9th Dispatch) Zhou Bangdao, Dai Xia, and Gu Zhaolan, Commissioners for Compulsory Education of the Ministry of Education, departed from Nanjing on the 9th. Zhou will inspect Anhui Province, Dai will inspect Jiangxi Province, and Gu will inspect Henan, Shaanxi, and Gansu Provinces.

(Anqing, 9th Dispatch) Zhou Bangdao, Inspector of the Ministry of Education, arrived in Anhui by the Songpu Steamship in the morning of the 9th. He is scheduled to begin inspecting primary and secondary school education in the provincial capital on the 10th, and then proceed to various counties in central, southern, and northern Anhui for separate inspections.

Budget for the Tax Academy This Year Reduced 156

(Nanjing, 9th Dispatch) After the relocation of the Tax Academy to Shanghai, the budget for the current fiscal year has been reduced to 96,000 yuan by the Ministry of Finance. The remaining 55,068 yuan, which is the difference between the reduced budget and the originally approved budget, has been approved by the Ministry of Finance to be included in the financial reserve fund for the current fiscal year for distribution.

Overview of Primary Education and Social Education in Jiangxi Province in Recent Years 157

The Ministry of Education has been compiling detailed statistics on primary and social education in various provinces and cities, and has already published figures up to the 21st year of the Republic of China in previous reports. We now present a summary of the most recent annual statistics on primary and social education in Jiangxi Province, compiled by the Jiangxi Educational Administrative Authorities after the 21st year of the Republic of China:

(A) Primary Education: There are a total of 5,900 schools and 9,400 classes in various counties and cities throughout Jiangxi Province. There are 201,227 male students and 43,418 female students, for a total of 244,645 students. There are 13,566 teachers and staff, and the expenditure is 2,022,704 yuan. (Note: The above figures are based on statistics from 81 counties and cities in Jiangxi. Hengfeng, Zixi, Ji'an, Yongxin, Xingguo, Yongxin, Lianhua, Chongyi, Shangyou, Ningdu, Guangchang, Shicheng, Ruijin, Huichang, Yudu, and Long'an were not included because they did not submit reports. The provincial capital (with a total of 85 schools, 546 classes, 12,702 male students, 6,950 female students, for a total of 19,651 students, 654 teachers and staff, and an expenditure of 409,651 yuan) is included in the combined statistics. County governments were not very familiar with the situation of provincial primary schools, and their reports were incomplete, so provincial primary schools were also included in the calculations for the provincial capital.

(B) Social Education: There are 1,946 social education institutions (1,091 public and 855 private), 1,325 classes (937 public and 388 private), 47,232 students (37,900 public and 9,332 private), 3,837 staff (2,404 public and 1,433 private), and an expenditure of 472,662 yuan (219,134 yuan public and 253,528 yuan private). If analyzed, the social education institutions include 803 public schools, 14 women's vocational supplementary schools, 88 public literacy centers, 6 physical education training centers, 2 commercial supplementary schools, 3 industrial supplementary schools, 50 agricultural supplementary schools, 1 opera and drum singing training class, 1 orphanage education institute, 1 other supplementary school, 31 music concerts, 3 physical education associations, 13 theaters, 125 parks, 170 public reading rooms, 7 cinemas, 10 other social education institutions, 179 public gymnasiums, 52 libraries, 34 education halls, 24 popular lecture halls, 316 public inquiry and writing centers, 1 public entertainment venue, 1 museum, 1 art museum, and 1 public education experimental area.

Yesterday was the date for the Family Friendship Gathering of Su Zhenhua Girls' Middle School. More than 700 guests attended. The discussion section was very valuable, with thorough discussions on the importance of guiding homework, supervising physical education and hygiene, and contacting parents and schools. Finally, the program was supplemented with many entertainment items, such as piano solos, labor songs, Buddhist songs, and the Tao of Man, making it even more brilliant.

Children's Educational Novel

Little Boy 164

— Original by Louiss M. Aloott, translated by Zheng Xiaocang

"I don't want to sleep. You said my boots are bad and I always slip," Robb was about to cry out loud, but he restrained himself with effort. Then he said, "If the mosquitoes (note) didn't bite me so much, I could sleep well and wait for Mama to come." This kind of pleading patience deeply touched Nan En's heart.

"Put your head on my lap, and I will cover you with my skirt; I am not afraid of the dark," Nan En said, sitting alone, trying to convince herself that she did not care about all the shadows and the strange sounds around her.

"Wake me up when she comes," Robb said, and in less than five minutes he had buried his head under Nan En's apron and was fast asleep.

The little girl sat alone for another quarter of an hour, looking around her anxiously, feeling that every second was like an hour. Suddenly, a faint white light shone from the top of the mountain, and she said to herself:

"I think the night is over, and morning is coming. I like to watch the sunrise, so I will wait for it. After the sun comes out, we can find our way home."

(Note) "Mosquitoes" is a mispronunciation of "mosquitoes."

U.S. Confirmed to Participate, Next Year's Olympics, Amateur Athletic Association Likely to Pass 165

(Reuters, New York, 8th) The All-America Amateur Athletic Union today passed with a vote of 61 to 55, confirming the United States' participation in next year's Olympics. The association is now preparing to protest to Germany through a compromise resolution regarding the unequal treatment of Jewish and Catholic athletes. The association has decided to no longer obstruct the United States' participation in the Olympics.

Yize Cup Athletics Postponed to Next Spring 168

Japanese and Russian expatriates requested postponement due to cold weather. Baihong Team agreed and decided to postpone to next spring.

The Baihong Track and Field Team, sponsored by the Jingwu Athletic Association, is an authority in the Chinese track and field world. They have participated in major sports events and won repeatedly. This year's Yize Cup Baihong Japanese-Russian International Triangular Tournament, Baihong has the most solid strength, with many war generals, and can be sure to win. Who knows, every Sunday is not beautiful, resulting in this wonderful track and field confrontation, repeatedly postponed. According to Kang Yong, the person in charge of the Baihong Team, told the Guoguang News Agency reporter yesterday that the Japanese and Russian expatriates recently requested the Baihong Team to postpone the international track and field competition to the spring of next year due to the cold weather. Baihong also allowed the request of Japanese and Russian expatriates to be held in the spring of next year because most athletes were taking exams at school and could not participate.

Commercial News

Finance, A Large Amount of Floating Shorts Emerge, Gold Price Almost Falls to 40 Yuan 172

—Resulting in a Fall of Three Yuan and Six Jiao—

Although the gold market stabilized yesterday due to the increase in the standard gold price, there was no shortage of supply to take advantage of the high price. Large bars were also sold slightly. After people's hearts stabilized, it gradually became tired. A large number of floating shorts emerged, once approaching the 40 yuan mark. In the morning, because the overseas silver market was flat in both the UK and the US, the silver price for Montri futures was unchanged or reduced by 1.5%, and the exchange rate fluctuated. The London raw gold rose by 1 dime and a half. The Central Bank's list was announced, with the UK and the US both flat, and the customs gold unit unchanged. The standard gold price was listed at 1147 yuan and 6 jiao, and people's hearts were slightly stable. Over-the-counter preparatory trading opened, rising to more than 45 yuan. The morning opening was slightly higher, and it was peaceful after the opening, with slight fluctuations. Mobil Oil Company bought US dollars, and buyers were more enthusiastic and rose slightly. HSBC Bank's list was announced, with the UK and the US both flat. At this time, there was a lot of hesitation. After entering, sellers gathered, and it was difficult to support, gradually declining. However, large buyers took advantage of the low price to accept strips, which was easy to pull up. The silver balance tax was announced and remained unchanged, and it was still sluggish. Later, due to the hardening of the foreign exchange market, the declining banks had some exits. Large buyers were waiting and watching, and there was a supply instead, gradually weakening. The prediction of the Indian silver shrinking by one anna was also not a big stimulus. Tongfengheng sold slightly. At noon, it was still tired. The after-market was stable, and people's hearts were still difficult to be encouraged. The selling wind was easy to stir up and step down. Although it struggled slightly due to the two shrinkages of two annas in Mumbai in the middle, the spot firms continued to post, and the swap spread still needed eight yuan. The congestion of the spot market has not yet eased, causing panic that this swap will be unfavorable to the long side, and the sellers are more fierce, so the long side collapsed and fell sharply, almost approaching the 40 yuan mark. Finally, it was slightly flat. The swap was posted by the long side for eight yuan yesterday. Today, the market conditions for one day are recorded as follows:

The morning opening was 1144 yuan and 9 jiao, a slight increase of 5 jiao compared to last Saturday. Shunmaoshenda Yongjin, Dadecheng Huixiang sells, and retreats from 5 yuan and 2 jiao to 4 yuan and 6 jiao. Oil Market: Soybean Oil Has Kerosene Flavor 183

Soybean Oil Is Likely to Rise, Not Fall, During the River Closure Period

The soybean oil market is in a situation of only rising and not falling. The rivers in the northeast are severely frozen, and the soybean oil mills in Niuzhuang, Shahe, and other places have stopped work and transportation as usual. Currently, the only source of goods is Dalian. Therefore, during this river closure period, there is little chance of falling prices. Yesterday, Niuzhuang oil shipped by steamer opened at 20.085 yuan, Shahe Qishan oil shipped by steamer opened at 20.00 yuan, Qishan oil shipped by sand boat opened at 19.90 yuan, Qingqi oil opened at 19.05 yuan, and soybean oil from this factory opened at 20.025 yuan. Currently, the city's inventory, excluding Dalian oil and factory oil, is approximately 1,000 large baskets and 2,000 small baskets. Recently, a dispute has occurred in the market regarding Dalian oil containing kerosene. It is recalled that the same thing happened two years ago, and it was settled after a Dalian representative came to Shanghai for verification. This time the problem has arisen again. The outcome will depend on how the industry deals with it.

White Tung Oil Rises and Falls 184

The foreign trader's route for white tung oil is endless. Half a month ago, spot goods were very short, and the Hankow market price once rose to 57 yuan per dan. Subsequently, cheap sales opened in Wanxian, Sichuan Province, and Changde, Hunan Province, and the Hankow market gradually loosened and fell. At the beginning of this month, it was still selling for 53.5 yuan, then 52.8 yuan, then 52 yuan. Yesterday, this port received a Hankow telegram stating that foreign traders had opened at 50 yuan. The previous rise was indeed caused by squeezing spot goods, so spot oil will be seen as relieved. It is falling back again. However, its rise and fall have had a significant impact on Zhejiang tung. At that time, Zhejiang tung once rose from 45-46 yuan to 52 yuan. Recently, it has fallen back to 46-47 yuan. However, since the foreign traders in Hankow have fallen to 50 yuan, it is possible that it will stabilize. Export goods are calculated in gold pounds. Since the shortening of the shilling, the current 50 yuan is equivalent to 40 yuan before our country's currency system was changed. After this, there will naturally be hope for the development of foreign trade. Moreover, tung oil exports are in a booming era, and they are flourishing.

Sugar Market: East Grain Opens at a Sharp Drop 185

Yesterday, the sugar market trended flat. The association's price for spot No. 24 coarse white sugar was 21.9 yuan, and the price for transit goods was 6.8 yuan, but no transactions were made. The price for this factory's refined white Zhinki No. 1 was 20.7 yuan, No. 2 was 20.4 yuan, No. 3 was 20 yuan, No. 4 was 19.8 yuan, and No. 5 was 19.6 yuan, with no changes. The Sugar Industry Cooperative Company auctioned 1,950 packages of Five Rams Guangdong coarse white sugar at a price of 21.8 yuan, with 1,000 packages traded. The remaining No. 2 and No. 4 refined white sugars were auctioned at the original price, and no transactions were made. The quoted prices for miscellaneous goods such as various grades of old goods and Qing goods have increased, but the trading firms are still observing and have not entered. East Red Sugar fell slightly, and MS brand was traded at 16.6 yuan. The quoted price for transit goods was 6.6 yuan. The quoted price for No. 8 white sugar rose by 0.05 yuan to 21.7 yuan, and the quoted price for transit goods was 6.65 yuan. The quoted price for No. 9 white sugar rose by 0.1 yuan to 21.55 yuan, and the quoted price for transit goods was 6.55 yuan. No transactions were made for any of them. Guokang high red sugar opened at 15.4 yuan, with dozens of packages traded.

Goods from North and South: Sichuan Preserved Vegetable Roots' Price Surges in Customer Demand 186

Sichuan preserved vegetable roots [zha cai] have recently seen limited sourcing due to high land prices making it difficult to be cost-effective. Consequently, the market price in Shanghai has increased by two or three yuan. Some suppliers have even quoted seventeen or eighteen yuan. However, as some traders and businesses had previously purchased at lower prices, they are now selling off their stock for profit, alleviating any concerns about shortages.

Textiles: French Serge Lining is Scarce, Price Increases 187

As the weather turns cold, the demand for overcoats has surged, leading to a dramatic increase in sales. However, shipments of French serge lining from foreign firms have ceased, resulting in a supply shortage in the Shanghai market. Both domestic and foreign warehouses have depleted their stock, causing the market to be very active. Based on current exchange rates and customs duties, the cost to import is approximately sixty cents per yard. Those holding inventory are now speculating and raising prices. Yesterday, A277 Old Brand French serge lining was sold at a net wholesale price of 57 cents per yard. Domestic Hongsheng goods were sold for 47 or 48 cents yesterday. Initially sold at 33 cents, Japanese French serge lining has now also experienced a sharp price increase to 42 or 43 cents. Buyers are seeking it everywhere for future use, but it is hard to find, making it a highly sought-after item in the recent woolen goods market.

Hardware: Five-Section Large Raw Leather is Scarce 188

Three-foot and six-foot large raw leather has become scarce since the military began purchasing it, especially the five-section pattern. Other patterns, from eight to ten sections, are also quite rare. The current market price for three- and four-section leather is eight yuan and twenty-five cents per picul. Five-section leather is out of stock, so the quoted price is nine yuan and fifty cents. Six- and seven-section leather is estimated at eight yuan and fifty cents, while eight- to ten-section leather is estimated at around nine yuan per picul.

Chronicles

Tidbits 189

— (A Cold Kiss)

Wu Zhilao once said: "The Executive Yuan is like the Earth God Shrine: with it, people still eat and sleep as usual. Without it, people still eat and sleep as usual. So there's no need to be anxious."

When Kang Youwei was dying, he told his two sons: "You should read more books by the ancients, and talk less about current affairs. This will both increase your knowledge and avoid unexpected dangers."

When Tang Shengzhi's National Revolutionary Army attacked Jiangxi from Hubei in 1926, they divided into two wings, one attacking Wuxue, and the other attacking Tianjiazhen. The 8th Army attacked Wuxue, but could not capture it after a long siege. Tang was very anxious, and asked his subordinates: "Why has Wuxue not been captured after so long? Which army is attacking?" The subordinates replied that it was the 8th Army. Tang suddenly realized, saying: "Using the 8th Army to attack Wuxue, since 'xue' [穴] means 'hole', and '8' [八] looks like a hole below, it is naturally difficult to overcome." Later, the 7th Army was reassigned to attack, and the city fell in a few days. This was also a strange event.

Poisons of Abyssinia 190

— Pei Yu

Italian soldiers introduced poison gas into the war to invade Abyssinia, but the Abyssinians themselves also had many potent poisons that could be used in exchange. In terms of function and effectiveness, their poisons were even more dangerous than poison gas. Abyssinian tribal people could extract juice from cacti and other plants to brew a strong poison. They could put this poison in water holes, poisoning enemy soldiers who drank it deep inland.

An Abyssinian chemist living in Addis Ababa (the capital of Abyssinia) knew the most details about deadly shrub poisons. He had recorded various poisons, listing an Abyssinian poison table, which contained many poisons made from plants unfamiliar to people elsewhere. For example, there was a poison called "Enga Bolobi", a powdered substance made from the dry roots of the "Enga Bolobi" shrub. If this poison powder was mixed in tobacco, the smoker would die after taking the second or third puff. The bulbs and fruits of several other plants could provide poisonous juice. If this poisonous juice was mixed into beer or boiled meat, unsuspecting people who ate it would suffer considerably, even losing their lives.

The most terrifying poison was the milky juice obtained from the seven-star candelabra-shaped cactus tree. Soldiers poured this poisonous juice into ponds, and within half an hour, all the fish in the pond floated to the surface, gasping for air. However, one thing that was astonishing and difficult to understand was that soldiers could catch and eat the fish floating on the surface gasping for air without being poisoned at all. The poison in a pond that had been poured with this juice was permanent, showing the toxicity. Once, a local did not know that poisonous juice had been poured into a pond a few days before, and used the water to wash his face while fishing. His companion quickly called him to stop, but it was too late. Water had splashed on his hands, face, neck, and arms. In less than twenty minutes, a large area of small blisters appeared on the skin where the water had splashed. His eyes closed, and his painful expression was frightening. His companion quickly washed him with clear water, but his eyes had already been damaged, and he was blind for more than a week. Therefore, when Italian soldiers crossed the Mareb River and invaded inland, they found that every mile they advanced increased the difficulty of their work.

The Innocent 191

Incense at the Yang Wang Temple 192

— Zhang Mengfei

There is a Yang Wang Temple in the northern part of Nanxiang City. It is built very solemnly. Inside is a statue of Yang Wang with a black face, which is very majestic. Every year on the day of the Zhongyuan Festival, boat gangs from all over come to welcome the gods and hold grand celebrations. This can be considered an annual event, which has been passed down for decades. Because Yang Wang has always protected them, giving smooth sailing, they have great faith and respect for him. However, starting this Spring Festival, there has been an unexpected surge in incense offerings at the temple. People from the northern district of Shanghai’s red-light district take the train to burn incense on the first and fifteenth days of the lunar month, making the Shanghai-Nanxiang train full of noisy chatter. According to them, a certain temple in Shanghai is no longer effective, but Yang Wang in Nanxiang is very effective. Burning incense once will definitely bring a considerable income, so everyone comes to burn incense sincerely.

The cost of burning incense is originally very high, especially for prostitutes! Donating some lamp oil, ten yuan or five yuan is originally nothing rare, as long as they are blessed in the underworld to receive one more big customer, a good fool.

Some people say that Yang Wang has had a stroke of luck this year—those who burn incense are a group of young and beautiful girls. When I heard it, I repeatedly said no...no...no...you are wrong. Do you know why prostitutes want to burn incense at Yang Wang's place? Isn't that god's statue black-faced? This can be understood very clearly, that is, ordinary gigolos are not willing to spend money, so let there be more people like Yang Wang.

Candle shops, prostitutes are also very superstitious. There is a Tianfu, they say that Tian gives blessing, the meaning is very good, so the candle business is very prosperous. There is a Wuchang, it is said that the word Chang is a homonym for the word sore, they are afraid of getting sores, so they are unwilling to buy, hehe, this can also be regarded as fortunate and unfortunate.

Little Western Paradise 193

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Twenty-Two: Knightly Words Move Rouge Lips, a Group of Sisters Convenes for Discussion; False Affection Startles Jade Wrists, a Suffering Girl Escapes Captivity

Sister-in-law Hu was so frightened that her face turned from red to green, and she forced a smile: "Oh! Sir, we don't know each other, and we have no grievances or hatred. Why are you treating me like this?" Bei Hai said: "If I knew you, I wouldn't let you do such a thing. As for whether there's hatred or not, you don't need to ask me. What hatred does your relative have with you, why did you sell his bones?" Sister-in-law Hu stood there blankly for a while, then she smiled: "Sir, you are doing this for the sake of the Zhu family's child. This has nothing to do with me. He has his grandmother and mother to decide, selling him to someone to be a servant. If you were as rich as Master Jia, wouldn't I have acted as matchmaker for you long ago? Their family is waiting for a son-in-law to save them from poverty, but if he can't save them from poverty, he can't be their son-in-law. What's the need for politeness?" As she said this, she curled her lips twice. Bei Hai couldn't help but feel a flutter in his heart when he heard these words, and his body stood frozen and unable to move. Sister-in-law Hu sneered, turned sideways, and rushed past him. By the time Bei Hai came to his senses, she had run far away. Bei Hai was given the cold shoulder. He couldn't catch up to her, so he could only lower his head and quietly walk back into the house. Zhi Qian stared at him for a while, then said: "What did you say to that woman?" Bei Hai gave a wry smile and said: "There's nothing to say to such an ignorant woman. The only thing to do is to use the law to deal with her." As he said this, he clenched his fist and slammed it heavily on the edge of the table. Zhi Qian looked at him like this and knew that he had run into a wall. He smiled slightly: "Young people are always quick-tempered. Actually, there are many unfair things in society, and we can only look at some and ignore others." Bei Hai put his hands back in his pockets, spun around in the room a few times, then lowered his head and sat down on the chair, sighing softly. Zhi Qian looked at the partition wall of the next room, pursed his lips, and whispered with a smile: "You really shouldn't have interrupted their merriment. Let him bring another girl for us to see. Are there so many poor people here that they all have to sell themselves?" Bei Hai said: "There aren't many people who sell themselves, but there are too many human traffickers. In the universe, the parties involved don't care, but it's always the middlemen who ruin things." The louder he spoke, the more the veins on his neck stood out. (374)

A Mother's Plea 194

— Zhang Zhenlu

When you tugged at my clothes and learned to speak,

You only clung to your mother's side all day long.

When you went out to school,

You only thought about finding a beautiful wife.

When you entered the bridal chamber,

You changed loved ones as soon as you got over it!

I worry about you, my sickly daughter,

I cherish you as my heart's treasure, my gold,

How much hardship I endured to raise you!

I remember when you were a child, you would respond to my every "mother".

Why now, after countless warnings, do you not heed my advice?

Sometimes, you roll your eyes and see your mother as a thorn in your side!

This attempts to combine the spirit and style of poetry, lyrics, and ballads into one, to make it easy to recite and sing, especially by heavily using existing colloquialisms, so that the public can be aware of it. This experimental work is intended to elicit sympathy from the contemporary audience. Perhaps there will be those who deride it as absurd, but I am prepared to accept their criticism! - Author's note.

Odds and Ends

Discussions on Artistic Trades 195

— Wan Lu

Our Eastern art has always been something that made Westerners speechless! Bamboo leaves and walnut boats have been passed down for a long time. I will not discuss those ancient skills, nor can I talk about so much. Now, I will just talk about the things I have seen personally, and that is enough to marvel at!

First, there is an ivory turning ring: On one side of a broad bean-sized ivory turning ring: A copy of the First Chibi Rhapsody was carved squarely and uprightly. Only black lines can be vaguely seen. Looking at it with a magnifying glass, it is a careful Su-style calligraphy, and the strokes are vivid and lifelike. On the other side: A picture of Su Dongpo's night tour of Chibi was carved. Although it can be seen that it is a landscape painting, under the magnifying glass, its levels and brushwork are indeed the painting method of the Three Wangs. The inscription is "Yu Xiaoxuan made in the capital." This Mr. Yu was still in Beiping in 1915 and 1916, so many people appreciated his art. Although there were several who could imitate him later, the details were slightly inferior, and the skill of the brushwork was inevitably different. This cannot be considered a superb skill?

Second, in 1919, at the banquet of Osi Ai Hadong, the owner of Shanghai's Ai Li Garden, I saw a silver cane: This silver cane was about two inches long, and the handle was inlaid with a yellow shell. According to the cracks of the shell, the natural demarcation, several lines of black characters were written on it. I don't remember the full text clearly; roughly: it describes a certain year in a certain province when a drought occurred, and Mr. Osi Ai Hadong generously donated a large sum of money to help the victims. The kindness of the righteous grain and benevolent soup saved countless lives. It expresses gratitude... etc. The inscription below is presented respectfully by the ×× Righteous Relief Association, and the calligraphy is also very accomplished. Compared to the carving of ivory by Yu Lanxuan, the writing is slightly larger, but it also needs to be identified with a magnifying glass, and Yu's carving is done with a knife, while it is written with a pen. What kind of pen can write such fine characters? And it is written on the rough shell! It is a pity that the person who wrote the characters did not leave his name.

Third, it is a fan pendant that I obtained in the inland: There are three stone seals of Tian Huangdong in the Beijing Ancient Artifacts Exhibition, which are made into three thin threads with the material itself and are connected together. Everyone was surprised to see it and thought it was the work of ghosts and gods. I personally obtained an ivory fan pendant in the inland of Anhui. It was a small gourd, like a white jade peanut. Some inscriptions and patterns were carved on the surface; after I bought it back, one day I wanted to wipe it clean, and I accidentally unscrewed the upper half of the gourd. I pulled out a thread that was more than three inches long from the gourd. It was even more strange! Four small trinkets were hanging on the thread: one was a honeycomb with several bees clinging to it, one was a flower basket with two peonies with complete branches and leaves inserted in it, one was a jue cup engraved with patterns of bells and tripods, and one was a small seal, which was also engraved with four square Zhuan script characters. Looking at it with a magnifying glass, it was the four characters "Liu Yin Ming Chuan". Only then did I understand the meaning of these objects, which was the implication of being granted the title of nobility and hanging the seal. Liu Mingchuan was from Anhui. He served as the Governor of Fujian and Taiwan during the late Qing Dynasty, and was granted the title of Baron for his military exploits. It was probably his subordinates who were currying favor with him. These small objects and a thread were all carved with the ivory itself. It was easy to pull them out, but it took a lot of effort to put them in. I don't know who's skill made this work of ghosts and gods? Unfortunately, I only had this item for a few years. Once, I encountered a very extraordinary change, and my life was almost lost. This item also disappeared.

A Kind of Big Business with Small Capital (Continued) 196

— Tian Xu Wosheng

If the labor of paper picking is changed to make crude bricks like bean cakes, then it can be done with half the effort. So I think this kind of division of labor and cooperation will definitely increase production. Other paper is afraid of being shelved and unable to be turned into money. If it is said to be pit paper, it is something that 400 million people use, and each sells to its own market. There is no fear that it will be shelved forever. Why should we hesitate not to do it.

(2) In any neighborhood, there must be many households. Taking Shanghai as an example, there are not uncommon to have one or two hundred households in a lane. If you register with the Utilizaiton Factory and take on the task of distribution, you only need to pay a deposit of fifty yuan to get seventy rolls to sell. This totals one thousand five hundred and forty Dao. Each Dao is sold for four and a half cents, and it can be sold for sixty-nine yuan and three cents. The payment only requires seventy cents per bundle, and there is still a five-yuan commission for every hundred yuan sold, which is in fact only a cost of forty-six yuan, five jiao and five cents, and you can get a profit of twenty-two yuan, seven jiao and nine cents. If you can turn it over twice a month, it is also considerable. In the beginning, we can also sacrifice a little, and send each household a roll with the words "Sold at this store" printed on the packaging paper. Once they try it, they will definitely feel that the product is good and cheap, no less than imported products, so they can sell it permanently, and there is no fear of others robbing it. This is very convenient, so why not do it?

The above method is a division of labor in manufacturing, a consumer cooperation in sales, and in fact a production and sales cooperation. I think it must be feasible, right?

(Note) The Utilization Factory can communicate directly with the Huishang Bridge in Wuxi

Shanghai Local Supplement of Shen Bao

The Issue of Adopted Sons 197

— Yu Yu Yu

Recently, two news stories about mothers beating their children to death occurred in Shanghai: one was Jiang Wang beating her biological daughter to death, and the other was Wang Cao beating her adopted son to death.

The love between mother and child is innate. There are many unfilial children in the world, but no parents who do not love their children. From the birth of each child to their growth and establishment of a career, parents exhaust their minds and efforts to raise them. The so-called parents' love for their children is meticulous. However, Jiang Wang beat her daughter to death because she cried easily and urinated and defecated at will, deviating from common sense and severely scolding and beating her to death. This cruel method makes me suspect that the woman may be suffering from severe mental illness? Because we can no longer argue for her with a proper reason.

Wang Cao beat her adopted son to death. An adopted son is not one's own flesh and blood, and being beaten to death by her, the situation is not as simple as the above. In addition to Wang Cao's case being revealed by the newspapers, I am afraid that there are still some similar murder cases happening secretly around us. Therefore, we put aside legal issues and open our eyes to look at the family system under this feudal society.

When a new daughter-in-law is about to enter the door, if she has not given birth after three years, the husband will quarrel and plan to take a concubine, and the in-laws will use the analogy of chickens that lay eggs to satirize her. The nosy experts will also use this as conversation material to pass the time; on the one hand, this is due to the habit of valuing sons over daughters in this society, and on the other hand, it is secretly promoted by the issue of inheritance, because our family system is organized by sons and inheritance. Having an inheritance without a son is the biggest concern of parents. Within the scope of possibility, the most convenient way is to take a concubine, because the reason that there are three forms of unfilial conduct, of which the worst is to have no descendants, is convincingly. But what about widows who have lost their husbands? The nephews of uncles and brothers are immediately adopted as sons. On the surface, the flesh and blood of brothers are indistinguishable, but family disputes arise from here, and tragic cases of abuse of adopted sons, even to the point of being beaten to death, follow one after another.

Sons are good because they are one's own. Now, a child who is separated by a layer of belly is adopted as a son in name. It is already difficult to maintain the state of ordinary mother and child, let alone the many twists and turns (inheritance disputes caused by the adoption issue) that make this pair of false mother and child incompatible. Therefore, the adopted mother has her reasons, and the adopted son has his grievances. Both sides are secretly running in opposite directions, but on the surface, they have to maintain the attitude of mother and child. Wang Cao beat her adopted son to death. The news does not provide many details, and we cannot guess the twists and turns, but it is conceivable that the adopted mother and the adopted son are easily as incompatible as water and fire. Then, if it results in being beaten to death, or other means that lead to death, can we say that it is an accidental reason? Wang Cao's case is just one that has been revealed to us. What method can we use to rescue the many adopted mothers and sons who are still fighting in the dark?

Setting Out, How Difficult! 198

— Especially

——One of the hardships of returning home through the snow

Days are not easy to pass when they are difficult, but they will not stop. The calendar is torn off one page after another, as if they do not care about their own process at all. Calculating it, it has been a full nine years.

For the death of my father, and for the oppression of being unable to endure hunger, I embarked on a vague future with tears in my eyes. I thought to myself, would this ease the burden of life? But when I thought of "prospects" and the reefs built inside, I was a little afraid, wasn't I? How would a sixteen-year-old child with two small furry fists wave in the iron-walled society?

I hardened my scalp and finally collided with the iron wall. Blood, sweat, and strength were covered by fatigue and soreness. One day, one month, one year, the torn calendars piled up under my feet. Unconsciously, I grew taller.

Autumn was driven away by a gust of cold north wind, and snow came, like goose feathers, covering the roofs and streets, estimating three or four inches. At this time, I lost my job.

——Where to go? Often, I am being questioned in my heart.

At that time, the situation was very urgent. The army filled the entire train and drove away. Panic hit everyone's heart. The nearby villages took the old and young and fled to the provincial capital, but the capitalists in the provincial capital fled to other provinces. What about the train? Don't think about it. It stopped running a long time ago. The air at the station was silent. Not to mention not having money, even if you have money, I'm afraid it's not easy to get out of that circle. Maybe it's "good luck," right? I thought

Page 16

I didn't expect that at that critical moment, there would be a salt truck preparing to leave from here to Tianjin. After several negotiations, I was lucky enough to get permission. This was simply an unparalleled honor for me!

The next night, everything was packed up. Outside the window, the wind was blowing very hard. Suddenly, the door opened——

——Really annoying, the train can't stop in this city, you——He hesitated for a moment, and I thought it would be better to take the early train to Zhengzhou tomorrow and wait, there will be someone to greet you at the station. The escort person ran over and said to me.

The calmed mood became chaotic again. I always felt that it was too risky. If a child who had never been far away from home did not have anyone to greet him at Zhengzhou Station, if the car could not run again, then, the scene in front of him was dark, how would he cope? Thinking about it, the thoughts became particularly chaotic. Finally, let's fight with the remaining courage that was on the line!

The heads of people at the station were scrambling around. From the platform to a very long path, I found the freight car. Obeying the escort person's instructions, I sent the luggage onto the freight car. And, I met the person I had asked for help in advance. Ah, there should be no problem, right? I thought to myself like this.

——You don't have to talk too much, remember. Mr. Sun, who had been entrusted, warned me.

Counting it, there were only twenty people in the car, but there was a lot of luggage. The piercing cold wind blew in from the doorless hole, my teeth were grinding, and goosebumps rose all over my body.

In the front of the car, the throat was strained and howled, once, twice, knowing that it was time to start running.

——Hey, where are you from? Several soldiers surrounded me and asked. I didn't respond. Then, they questioned me even more urgently. It was really terrible. They asked me first, and there was no opportunity to even consider. It seemed impossible not to speak——

——Me? I am from ×××. I finally replied.

——Okay, get down, get down! Without explanation, I was pushed down and stood beside the rails. Mr. Sun told me to buy a ticket for third class, and he would be responsible for the luggage. See you again after Zhengzhou. When speaking, it seemed to blame me for being nosy.

The third-class car was full of people. I stood by the door of the toilet, my heart rising and falling uneasily, thinking about the luggage, thinking about my hometown, thinking about the prosperous commercial port, and also thinking about the ambush in the commercial port,... I was at a loss.

What time did the car actually leave? I didn't feel it at all.

Snowy Night 199

— Shen Wu

At dusk, we were warming ourselves by the fire inside the house, burning a dry, withered twig we had picked up from the countryside. The flames flickered gently in the dark room, casting a red glow on everyone's faces.

There were no windows in the house, and it was surrounded by stacks of wooden crates that had carried foreign goods, and bulky local products, piled so densely that the house seemed to be fortified like a trench. The air could barely find any space to seep in, and the main door was tightly shut. The fire crackled as it burned the dry twigs, sometimes shooting out sparks like shooting stars. We all stared silently at the fire, without speaking. The quiet silence was unsettling. Yet no one dared to break it, and we just sat there blankly.

Snow was falling, like cotton, and we could still vaguely see people walking in the snow through the cracks in the door. Slowly, a dark figure blocked the small opening in the doorway, and we faintly heard heavy footsteps. Everyone's gaze immediately shifted from the fire to the door. We listened as the footsteps gradually approached, step by step.

A strangely monotonous knock made us aware of the terrifying journey in this snowy night.

The door opened, and unexpectedly it was not Old Ge, but the young, chubby Qin Fu, a partner from Longchang Mountain Goods Store. He secretly breathed a sigh of relief, thinking, "It would be terrible to have to rush on the road tonight! The snow is especially heavy today, and the mountain road will be difficult to travel at night." But in everyone's minds, no one dared to decide whether to endure the night road.

Old Man Zhu made room for Qin Fu to sit down. His body was covered in snowflakes, which immediately melted into water droplets upon touching the flames. So he shook himself a few times to let the water drip down, and then slowly sat down.

With one more person in the room, it didn't seem as deathly silent as before. Everyone's eyes were focused on Qin Fu, as if trying to find something to talk about. Old Man Zhu closed his eyes, thinking about something. After a moment, he suddenly let out a long sigh, looked at Qin Fu, and then opened his dry mouth to say:

"Qin Fu, your store doesn't have to rush at night in snowy weather, right? I heard from Old Ming that there's no need to rush mountain goods at night in winter... Your boss is really good, not making things difficult for his partners in snowy weather. We can't do that, we rush day and night. I don't know what tonight will be like? I'm too useless, still without any success after being a porter for decades. It's really dangerous to walk in snowy weather. If my blood weakens for a moment and I fail, then it's over! It's not good to live well, but I should at least die well. I really don't want to die in the mountains and become a mountain god... Alas, it's hard to say, I've seen these things with my own eyes, Uncle Lin Er died like that... It's really scary to talk about..." He paused and then fell silent again.

Qin Fu lowered his head, watching the flames flicker, and poked at the twigs with his hand, as if wanting to raise his head to answer Old Man Zhu, but he only glanced at him vaguely and then lowered his head again without saying a word.

Everyone continued to sit quietly. Song Sen stretched out his hands, yawned, and stretched, looking a bit tired. Old Man Zhu closed and opened his eyes from time to time, looking at our expressions, and then lowered his head in thought.

The night gradually passed, and the snow seemed to be getting heavier. The footsteps outside the door became sparse.

The flames of the dry twigs were not as strong as before, and our toes felt a bit cold, stiff, itchy, and painful. Song Sen couldn't bear the silent suffering and wanted to sleep. So Qin Fu decided to go back.

I opened the door for Qin Fu, and he flashed his flashlight at the street. The snow had thickly covered the ground. He took a few steps and suddenly cried out "Ah!" and turned back, calling my name, "Old Cen!"

Thinking something had happened to him, I grabbed Old Man Zhu's hand, felt for a gun by my side, and ran out.

Qin Fu shined the flashlight on the snow. It was a corpse, already tightly pressed down by the snow, and the person was no longer breathing. Old Man Zhu shook his graying head and sighed, "Alas, still a hard life—"

Movie

"Hero of the Hour" to be Released Soon 205

Yi Hua Film Company's latest and most valuable production, a problem drama dissecting the causes of the decline of industry and commerce, a full dialogue sound singing feature film "Hero of the Hour," will be released soon at the Jincheng Grand Theater. Regarding this film, with director Ying Yunwei holding great confidence first, and the supporting audience placing sincere attention behind, there is no doubt that it will resonate throughout Shanghai. Moreover, the film not only has a profound and sharp dissection of the rise and fall of Chinese industry and commerce over the past fifty years, but also a clear introduction and systematic narration of the large number of foreigners coming to China over the past fifty years, their active investment in various businesses in China, the impact and waves this has caused on Chinese society, and the economic and cultural invasion and changes it has undergone. Because the director is quite adept at using film techniques, it is filled with a tense, enthusiastic, and stimulating atmosphere from beginning to end, able to tightly grasp the psychology of every audience member, causing the audience's excited emotions to rise and even explode in uncontrollable feelings as the plot unfolds. In particular, the conditions of Shanghai streets and the clothing customs of Shanghai men and women from all walks of life forty to fifty years ago are all shown in this film, so it can also give the audience a sense of recollection, like tasting a remonstrative fruit with endless aftertaste, revealing a knowing smile in the midst of the tense atmosphere.

A scene from Chaplin's new film "Modern Times" 206

Another amazing masterpiece after "City Lights"

"Human Relations"—A Worldly Work 207

No matter which aspect you look at it from, the success of "Human Relations" has indeed won great glory for the Chinese film industry.

In terms of plot, this unfolds the story of four generations of a family, explaining the true meaning of familialism through extremely complex human relationships. Chinese people have always been rich in family ideology. Due to the deep-rooted nature of this ideology, they gradually fall into narrowness, only knowing about the family and forgetting that there is a larger society existing outside the family. Society, and even the country, is dominated by this narrow family ideology, thus experiencing a great impact. "Human Relations" grasps this theme and seriously explains that everyone must extend their love for the family to all of humanity. In "Life," playwright Zhong Shigen once shouted the slogan of saving children. In "Human Relations," he raises this righteous cry again.

In terms of direction, the most noteworthy thing is that every shot has a new and innovative creation. In any small segment, one can see that the director has put in extremely hard work. The arrangement of characters, the creation of atmosphere, and the use of shots are all original—which will amaze you, amaze you that such an amazing work can be produced under China's backward mechanical technology.

Speaking of actors: this is enough to be proud of everything. It brings together the elite of Lianhua's stars, creating the only miracle after "The Big Road." Everyone has achieved balanced development, and all contribute their most skilled acting skills. Watching such a film, just in terms of its actors, is enough to satisfy people.

Of course, photography, scenery... and everything else has amazing achievements.

This is the glory of the Chinese film industry.
