Shen Bao Architectural Weekly

Exploration of Ancient Bath Garden Architecture (Below) 208

— Sun Zongwen

—One of Rome's National Architectural Art Masterpieces—

Roman bath garden architecture is divided into two types: 1. Small bath gardens, 2. Large bath gardens. The former was built from the Republic era, called Balnae, imitating the Greek system, with a capacity of hundreds of people; in the city of Rome, there were no less than six hundred of these small bath gardens, but most were private, so they can also be called "private bath gardens." The latter was built from the Empire era, called Thernae, with a capacity of thousands of people, with about one hundred in the entire city. Because they are public in nature and funded by the state, they can also be called "public bath gardens." In the history of world architectural art, the former has little influence, and the latter has great influence. Therefore, when architectural researchers speak of Roman bath gardens, they mostly refer to public large bath gardens. Here, we can see that the appearance of this type of architecture at that time really gave people a good impression, just like the appearance of temple architecture in the Greek era! Deeply imprinted in our minds, giving us an understanding of how ingenious, precious, and great the ancient architectural art was...

The Roman bath garden was founded by Scipia Apricanus, the marshal of the Punic War, but the work was not perfect. Until Rome became a country, the bath garden was only for preparation. Until the imperial era, it changed the old view of the past, adding extravagance and seeking pleasure at will. Therefore, the function of the bath garden also changed from the purpose of hygiene to a place of extravagant pleasure-seeking; this is the general history of Roman bath garden architecture.

Roman public bath gardens are also like modern clubs, because their purpose is not only for people to bathe, but also for people to use for recreation. Therefore, in addition to a part of the bath pool building, there are also parks, sports grounds, theaters, rest rooms, libraries, and various markets, all built in. As for the form of the bath pool, it is not uniform, with square, rectangular, round, and elliptical shapes. The buildings along the coast of the bath pool have huge rooms, which are dressing rooms for changing clothes after bathing. Outside the dressing room, there is a colored column cloister, circulating throughout the garden. In addition to hot and cold water, the bath pool water also has perfume for women, and the bath pool in the palace also has milk. In the movie "Spring Colors of the Roman Palace," it is said that "the emperor and queen bathed together in hundreds of buckets of milk." From this, we can know that the pride, luxury, and licentiousness of Rome at that time can be used as a powerful and ironclad proof.

The materials for Roman bath garden architecture are mostly valuable. The inlay work in the garden is made of various colored pearls and jades, shining brightly. The bath pools are made of gold, silver, jade, and crystal clear white stone. The attached sculptures, paintings, flowers, and figures are lifelike. The columns and colonnades of the cloister are decorated with gorgeous colors, adding a layer of magic to this magnificent bath garden! Making visitors feel dazzled and fascinated, with a strange idea of entering a dreamlike state!

The Roman people's love of bathing is really like the lower-class people's love of drinking tea in China now. Romans entering the bath garden is equal to Chinese people going to the teahouse. And the bath pool water is cold and hot, so some people have tasted only the hot pond, and Wen Jingliang Pond is said to be good, enjoying it endlessly, and some have entered the garden since childhood, from batches to old age, happily forgetting to return. In addition, various domestic and foreign news are gathered in the dressing room in the surrounding area, forming friendships daily, listening to new sayings from time to time, directly like a fair exhibition. Because of this, the magic of the bath garden is becoming greater day by day. As for the greatest representative work of the bath garden, it is the Emperor Caracalla, which has been destroyed, but later generations see its ruins like a city site of more than ten miles, and the greatness of its project can be imagined! Commentators say that the Roman bath garden is enough to represent the peak of Rome and also enough to invite the downfall of Rome; although there are many reasons for the downfall, the bath garden is also one of them. Since the Germanic forest barbarians came out, Rome also announced its demise; once Rome was destroyed, the large living room in the bath garden was changed into a Christian church. The gold and stone treasures in the garden are also in the museums of various European countries. The large stones of the bath garden were changed into coffins for certain Christians. Because bath garden architecture was a representative of the national architectural glory in the era of its full power; and at the time of the overthrow of the clan society, it was also enough to show the warning of sin. From this, we can know that buildings can not only represent the rise and fall of a country, but also influence the rise and fall of a country!

When did China's bath garden begin? It is really impossible to verify. But we know that it already existed in the Tang Dynasty. And great masterpieces have appeared one after another. The most famous of these is the "Huaqing Pool" built on Mount Lishan, south of Lin'an County, Shaanxi. The pool contains hot springs. When Emperor Taizong of the Tang Dynasty first built it, it was called Yiquan Palace. Emperor Xuanzong changed it to Huaqing Palace, and the pool was also named Huaqing Pool.殿臺 were arranged around the pool, and hundreds of departments and public officials' residences were also set up. The magnificence of the building can also be imagined! Moreover, there is also a fragrant and romantic story in it!

China's bath gardens, just like Roman bath gardens, are mostly built inside palaces, exclusively for the enjoyment of emperors and queens. From the "Tang Hui Yao," we can see the following record:

"...Dezong said to Pei Yanling that the bath hall palace where he lived would crush it if it was not easily changed..."

Also, from "Bai Juyi's Poems," we can find two sentences:

"Accustomed to seeing greenhouse trees, well-versed in bath hall flowers"

From the above two paragraphs, we can know how prevalent bath gardens were in palaces at that time. Unfortunately, there is no special book to record its architectural details, and we have no way to explore it.

As for what the folk architecture of our country's bath gardens was like? Then we can know some general information from the record in the book "Yangzhou Painted Boat Record": To make the end of this article!

"The wind of the bath pool was opened in Guo Tang of Shaobo Town, and later Zhang Tang outside Xuning Gate imitated it, and used white stone as the pool, more than ten feet square, with several large and small grids, the larger one near the pot, the water is hot as a large pool, and the smaller one with not very hot water is a baby pool." (End)

Panoramic View of the Municipal Hospital in the Central Area of Shanghai 209

The Municipal Hospital, designed by architect Dong Dayou and built by Lugenji Construction Company, has been completed in full. The house was ground breaking by Mayor Wu on New Year's Day this year. The work lasted for more than ten months. All building materials are top-notch goods. The use of block flooring in the hospital is especially suitable. It is said that it was undertaken by the local Meihe Foreign Company. The total cost is about 440,000 yuan. Because Lugenji, the contractor of the house, was also in charge of building the National Music Conservatory next to the Shibanjian Bridge on Guofu Road in Nanjing, Mr. Lu Genquan, the owner of the factory, is currently signing the contract in Beijing and will return to Shanghai this Friday to actively decorate the interior of the house so that it can be completed and opened as soon as possible to benefit the citizens.

Architectural Jargon (Twenty-one) 210

— Mei Zhenhuan

—About the Use in Construction Sites—

Lu Fei——What is Lu Fei? It is the thing made of Mao Chai tubes that ordinary people call Lu Xi. In the construction site, the use of Lu Fei used to depend almost entirely on it. Now, because the engineering management authorities (referring to the concession) have seen that Lu Fei is easy to catch fire. Except for those that cannot be avoided and must be used. It is generally prohibited. However, when building houses in the inland, those small-capital bosses often still use Lu Fei to build the facade and wall of the tent room and material room (detailed earlier) in order to save expenses.

Oil Taa——The meaning of Oil Taa. It is another name for oil paper made by soaking mulberry paper in tung oil. It is used to sandwich in the inner layer of Lu Fei. (One sheet of oil Taa is sandwiched between two sheets of Lu Fei) in order to prevent rain water from being soaked when covering the roof.

Han Zi——A thing made of bamboo pieces sharpened into a sharp point at both ends. The thing shaped like an arrow is called Han Zi. It is used to flatten Lu Fei. (What is called not Lu Fei. It is to cover the roof or wall. Han Zi is used to make it flat).

Bamboo Strips——Using bamboo heads to build scaffolding. There are also many names such as Chong Tian, ​​Qi Kang, Ding Cheng, and Heng Leng. But its method is not like wooden scaffolding with several lead wires wrapped tightly. It is to tie each place firmly with bamboo strips. Bamboo strips are thin strips seven or eight feet long made of bamboo cyan (that is, the cyan side. The other side is called bamboo yellow.). It must be immersed in water when used. Because the nature of bamboo strips is too dry, it is not easy to tie the joints of the scaffolding firmly. The remedy. Just soak it in water before. It is more convenient to tie it up. (To be continued)

Family Bonds 212

— Da Kang

The Glory of Chinese Cinema

In the past twenty years, China has only produced one such "Family Bonds," a uniquely bold work. It is fully deserving of the solemn title of "Cinematic Art."

No one in the domestic film industry has ever dared to attempt a script with such a broad scope, encompassing stories spanning seventy or eighty years, from the first generation to the fourth, from family love to human love. Although its name is "Family Bonds," it is not limited to narrow familialism but advocates breaking away from familialism and extending this love to all of humanity.

Stringing together the stories of four generations under one roof, it depicts the vicissitudes of a family and embodies the so-called "human love"—the greatest and purest love in the universe. This is the essence of "Family Bonds."

"Family Bonds" is written by the renowned playwright Zhong Shigen. His previous works, such as "Humanity," "City Nights," and "Life," were all masterpieces. In this play, he continues to use complex structures to express his lofty ideals. From this, one can glimpse his spirit of speaking out for humanity and the masses.

Directing such a complex play is exceptionally difficult, but the director of this film was able to handle it with ease, using his special techniques and a very solemn tone to organize this intricate play in a methodical manner. In every shot and every scene, you can find new and special creations. Sometimes, even in very ordinary scenes, his techniques can touch the depths of the human soul.

For the actors, the most outstanding talents of Lianhua were selected. Each of them gave their best performance. Lianhua used ninety percent of all its actors to fully produce this film.

"Family Bonds" is undoubtedly worthy of being recorded as a glorious achievement in the Chinese film industry.

The Aesthetic "Family Bonds" 213

— Wanderer

With China's top-tier director, taking over a year, spending nearly 100,000 yuan, and gathering the energy of Lianhua's twelve major stars to write about the historical process of Chinese society's evolution in the forty years before and after the revolution, this alone is enough to stand out in the film industry and look down on everything else.

What's more...

The correctness of the "Family Bonds" consciousness is not only unprecedented in the film industry but also, in a social sense, starts from the love of parents and children and aims for the love of humanity. This kind of ethical view is truly an eternal truth, and its greatness is far beyond the reach of ordinary, impromptu writers.

In terms of scenery, the architecture is magnificent, and the furnishings are luxurious and splendid. The beauty of embellishing the screen is self-evident, and its contribution to promoting China's inherent art cannot be ignored.

The selection of outdoor scenes is ingenious. The misty rain of Jiangnan is already intoxicating. The scenery of water and mountains stretches for thousands of miles. After watching it, one's feelings are refreshed.

The consistency of the actors' performances is also a feature of this film. It is purely won by depth and is extremely touching, giving viewers the impression that they cannot avoid it. There is probably no one who can watch it without shedding tears.

In short, "Family Bonds" is not only an unprecedented miracle in the history of Chinese cinema, but the world film industry will also be shocked by it.

— Wen

The kind mother on the screen, the comforter of countless orphans, has an unprecedented performance in "Family Bonds." All of her past achievements have been satisfactory, but in "Family Bonds," she takes it to the next level. Especially when announcing that their grandson has embezzled public funds, her expression can be said to move heaven and earth and make ghosts and gods weep.

Mei Lin

A beautiful and delicate little girl, who became a daughter-in-law who bowed her head and endured insults, with a taste of chastity and tranquility.

It is rare for a film to have so many brilliant stars, and they are all veteran warriors who have been through countless battles. This alone shows its greatness and beauty.

Speaking of the art of directing, "Family Bonds" can be rightly called the only creative masterpiece in the history of Chinese cinema, and we believe that this film will definitely win unparalleled glory for our film industry.

This is what we deeply know: Lianhua spent three years preparing for the completion of this film, one year in production, a significant amount of money and brainpower, and almost all of Lianhua's energy was focused on this film.

The fact that "Family Bonds" can be shown at the Grand Theatre and will be promoted to the world at the same time is the most gratifying thing in the history of Chinese cinema, and it can also be said that the film has achieved victory after hard work!

My Thoughts on "Family Bonds," Opening Next Week at the Grand Theatre 216

— Tu Long

"Heaven is the norm, earth is the righteousness, and the people are the actions."

This is indeed a rare work in the Chinese film industry!

From the perspective of plot and theme: It depicts the deeds of four generations—great-grandparents, grandparents, parents, and children—in a family over several decades. However, these decades were precisely when Eastern and Western cultures were in rapid contact, and social attitudes and standards changed several times. The psychology and behavior of Chinese society during these decades also had various different forms. In particular, shortly after the initial contact between Eastern and Western cultures, old social attitudes and standards were about to be destroyed, and new social attitudes and standards were not only not yet established but were still in a state of confusion where everyone insisted on their own views. At this time, people wanted to escape the old shackles, but after escaping the old shackles, "where to go?" Since the question of "where to go" could not be resolved, people naturally fell into confusion, or went astray. Calmly speaking, I am afraid that more people went astray than hesitated in those years!

What "Family Bonds" indicates to those who have gone astray is: Come back, lost sheep! However, what is indicated to the lost sheep here is not the old road they came from, but a right path in front of the old road, which is to say: Dedicate yourself to the broad masses.

From the name of this play, it is clear that the theme must be to teach "filial piety." That's right, not wrong at all, teach filial piety, but this is not teaching people to learn "cutting one's arm to cure a parent" or "worshipping mountains and praying to Buddha for a parent's longevity," but rather teaching people to be "inhumanly" filial. Instead, it teaches people to be filial in a natural, human way.

"The beginning of human love is based on a kind of infant love, that is, the natural love between parents and children. The universe is eternal, and this love is also eternal."

Here, "filial piety" is not explained as an absolute duty of children to their parents. In particular, it is not explained as a private thing in a parent-child relationship (note: relationship). It is explained as a common emotion between humans, which is a part of the broad human love that occurred earlier due to convenience.

Because of the difference in explanations, there are significant differences in the ways of practicing filial piety.

Explaining filial piety as a private possession of the parent-child relationship and as an absolute duty of children to their parents means that, first, parents may not be kind, but children cannot be unfilial; second, as long as so-called "filial piety" is practiced, the means used do not matter. A robber may kill and loot, but he can gain the name of a filial son for providing delicious food to please his parents.

It is not like this here!

It says that "filial piety" (actually love) is a common emotion among humans and is the foundation for promoting broad human love. Therefore, the principle of parental love and filial piety arises in the family. Externally, it is "respect the elders of others as you respect your own, and care for the children of others as you care for your own." Loving others is being filial to one's parents. Harming others to be filial to one's parents is not only not considered filial but also considered rebellious.

This ethical view can be said to be "unchanging for a hundred generations and applicable to all seas."

From a technical point of view: With a straightforward story, it arranges decades of time and dozens of actors. It is a more difficult task to manage in terms of systematic organization, and the director has skillfully handled this time and these characters. In theory, he adopted the viewpoint of neo-symbolism, enthusiastically using some materials that seem to have little to do with the topic but are actually the most powerful. Not only does it add some help to the writing of the story, whether explicitly or implicitly, I am afraid that it is also a brand new type in the field of Chinese cinema.

As mentioned earlier, what "Family Bonds" shows to people is "human love," and the director grasped this point. Originally, this so-called human nature is a virtue unique to human beings. Readers should not misunderstand that the author has some idealistic color. No, the so-called human love is not something that falls into the realm of human consciousness out of thin air, but the result of years of human cultural accumulation, the sublimation of primitive love.

The director deliberately described this central consciousness, and the great and painful scenes attracted the viewers so much that they almost felt as if they were in it and were deeply moved. Although there are inevitably some preachy elements, it is gratifying that, like Bai Juyi's poems, even if it is preaching, it does not feel dry and dull at all.

In particular, the greatness and beauty of the pictures give viewers great appeal, and for its greatness and beauty, I would rather abandon the magnificent architecture and take its poetic natural scenery. Even if it is just water, clouds, birds, and trees, without having to savor the deep meaning it contains, just evaluating it from an aesthetic point of view, its beauty is by no means something that ordinary hands can use. As for the vast mountains and forests, the white lambs freely jumping and gnawing, the setting sun reflecting its afterglow from the horizon, and the shepherd climbing high and calling out, it will make you inevitably think of the sentence "The sun is setting"!
